> 1

### Assistant
> You’re looking at a bunch of “stack recipes” people throw around (Vercel + Render + Supabase, etc.). They can work, but for **your** case system the right choice is driven by two non-negotiables:
> 
> 1) **Low-ops, low-surprise billing** (you’ve already been burned by “it worked yesterday” platforms)  
> 2) **A live database + a static viewer (Quartz) that can be regenerated deterministically**
> 
> Here’s the straight answer, based on current provider realities.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## The real state of the world (as of late 2025 / early 2026)
> 
> ### Supabase: good “live DB + auth + API,” but Free pauses
> Supabase Free includes unlimited API requests, up to 50,000 MAU, 500MB DB, etc., but **Free projects pause after 1 week of inactivity** and you only get **2 active projects**. citeturn0search0  
> That’s manageable (heartbeat ping), but it’s a constraint.
> 
> ### Fly.io: not “free tier” anymore
> Fly’s own docs now explicitly state **there is no free tier** (only trial/credits), and overages can bill. citeturn0search1turn0search13  
> For “I don’t want billing surprises,” Fly is not your first choice.
> 
> ### Render: Free exists but is limited/sleepy
> Render Free has real constraints and free compute-hour rules; free services are not meant for always-on “production” backends. citeturn0search2turn0search14
> 
> ### Vercel: good frontend hosting, but limits exist
> Vercel Hobby limits are real (deploy size, etc.). Great for frontend; just don’t rely on it for heavy backend work. citeturn0search7turn0search3
> 
> ---
> 
> ## For your case system: what you actually need
> 
> You do **not** need a “backend server” for Quartz or for generating pages most of the time.
> 
> You need:
> - **Live DB** to track tasks, responses, disputes, statuses (so it doesn’t fall apart)
> - **A scheduled job** to pull from DB and generate Quartz markdown pages (status dashboard, response tracking, etc.)
> - **Static hosting** for Quartz (already working)
> 
> That’s it.
> 
> So the “backend” is not a server; it’s a **sync job**.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Recommended stack (minimal moving parts, maximum reliability)
> 
> ### Option 1 (best fit): Cloudflare Pages (Quartz) + Supabase + Cloudflare Worker (sync job)
> **Why this wins:**
> - Quartz stays static and fast on Cloudflare
> - Supabase is your live system of record (tasks/complaints/responses)
> - Worker runs on a schedule, pulls data from Supabase, generates `STATUS.md` + `RESPONSE_TRACKING.md`, commits to repo (or writes to KV/R2 if you prefer)
> 
> This avoids “backend hosting” entirely.
> 
> **Caveat:** You still need to keep Supabase Free from pausing (heartbeat). citeturn0search0
> 
> ### Option 2: Cloudflare Pages + Supabase + GitHub Actions (sync + build)
> Even simpler than Workers:
> - GitHub Action runs every X hours
> - Pulls from Supabase
> - Writes/updates Quartz markdown pages in repo
> - Builds Quartz (if needed)
> - Pushes
> 
> This is very stable and auditable. Also keeps all outputs versioned.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## What about Render / Fly / Vercel + backend?
> Use them only if you are building a true app backend (file uploads, complex processing, websockets). For your “case ops DB + generated dashboards,” they’re unnecessary complexity.
> 
> - **Fly.io**: not free tier anymore; billing risk. citeturn0search1turn0search13  
> - **Render**: fine, but free tier constraints and sleep behavior aren’t what you want for “always available case ops.” citeturn0search14turn0search2  
> - **Vercel**: keep it frontend-only if you use it at all. citeturn0search7turn0search3
> 
> ---
> 
> ## MongoDB vs Supabase for you
> MongoDB is fine technically, but it creates immediate questions you don’t want:
> - Where’s auth?
> - How do you do row-level security?
> - How do you quickly build “tables” views?
> - How do you generate structured status pages?
> 
> Supabase gives you:
> - Postgres (structured)
> - Auth
> - RLS policies
> - Studio UI (phone-friendly)
> - Easy “ops state” tracking
> 
> For a case management system: **Supabase wins**.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## The “simple live interface” you asked for
> You already have Quartz for viewing evidence.
> 
> What you need is a **Case Ops Console** that is live and dumb:
> 
> - Table view of tasks
> - Filter by phase/status
> - “Next 5 actions”
> - “Waiting / blockers”
> - Complaint/response tracker
> 
> You can get this two ways:
> 
> ### Fastest: Supabase Studio (no build)
> Use Studio as your “GUI” today.  
> It will not break. It works on mobile. It’s already there.
> 
> ### Better: Tiny Cloudflare page (read/write) using Supabase Auth
> One small React app hosted on Cloudflare Pages that logs in and edits tasks.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Decision you need to make (I’ll drive it either way)
> 
> ### If your priority is “don’t fall apart”
> Do this:
> 1) Supabase tables + RLS  
> 2) Use Studio as GUI  
> 3) GitHub Action sync generates Quartz status pages
> 
> ### If your priority is “I want a slick dashboard”
> Do this:
> 1) Supabase tables + RLS  
> 2) React dashboard on Cloudflare Pages  
> 3) GitHub Action sync still generates Quartz status pages
> 
> Either way: Quartz remains the record.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Your “backend” answer
> You said “Backend: don’t know.”
> 
> For this system, your backend is one of:
> - **Cloudflare Worker cron job** (preferred if you want Cloudflare-first)
> - **GitHub Actions scheduled job** (preferred if you want simplest + auditable)
> - **Render/Fly server** (only if you need always-on API beyond Supabase)
> 
> Most likely, you do **not** need a server backend.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Next step (no questions, just pick)
> Tell me which one you want:
> 
> 1) **Supabase Studio + GitHub Action sync (fastest, strongest, least fragile)**  
> 2) **Supabase + React dashboard on Cloudflare Pages + GitHub Action sync (nicer UI)**  
> 3) **Full backend server (only if you insist)**
> 
> Pick 1/2/3 and I will give you the exact Gemini prompt + file set + RLS policies + deployment steps.

### User
> I love your option two, but what if i need to work mobily or dont have a reliable machine and want to upload new docket documents, download the template for a motion to my phone update the motion and upload it to my case then file with online case, what if we do make this a full app but just try to keep it simple without too many bells for quick deployment. priority is, this desktop blows up, (laptop is alredy dead) and im down to my phone or a library computer i can continue the case without too many issues from executive funciton

### Assistant
> Yes. If your constraint is “my desktop could die any day and I might be stuck on a phone or library computer,” then a **full (but simple) case app** is not optional — it’s your continuity plan.
> 
> You can do this without bells and whistles. The trick is designing it so it works under **low executive function** and **unreliable devices**.
> 
> Here’s the architecture and the minimal feature set that actually solves your scenario.
> 
> ---
> 
> # The goal (operational, not pretty)
> From **any** device (phone, library PC), you can:
> 
> 1) Upload new docket docs (PDFs, images, audio/video)  
> 2) Auto-log them (date, source, tags, phase, evidence ID)  
> 3) Download a motion template to your phone  
> 4) Edit it in the tool you already have (Google Docs / Word mobile)  
> 5) Upload the final PDF back into the case  
> 6) Generate a “filing packet” export (motion + exhibits list + attachments)  
> 7) Track next steps and deadlines live
> 
> Quartz stays your “read/search/browse” layer, but the app becomes your **working cockpit**.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Recommended stack (simple, mobile-first, low ops)
> ### Frontend (PWA): Cloudflare Pages + React
> - Works on phone
> - “Install to Home Screen”
> - Offline caching for UI
> 
> ### Backend: Supabase (Postgres + Auth + Storage)
> - Database for tasks, filings, evidence index, templates, activity log
> - Storage buckets for PDFs and media
> - RLS for security
> 
> ### “Glue” automation: Supabase Edge Functions OR Cloudflare Workers
> - Generate IDs
> - Write metadata
> - Produce exports (zip / packet builder light)
> - Optional: sync a status page into Quartz later (not required to operate)
> 
> This avoids running your own server. That’s what keeps it deployable fast.
> 
> ---
> 
> # What you need in the app (MVP modules)
> No fluff. Just the modules that prevent collapse.
> 
> ## 1) Inbox Upload (the most important screen)
> **Phone-first upload pipeline:**
> - Upload file(s)
> - Choose Source: “MyCase / Clerk / Email / Screenshot / Other”
> - Choose Type: “Docket”, “Evidence”, “Draft”, “Photo/Video”
> - Choose Phase: 01–06
> - Add quick tags (optional)
> - Save
> 
> On save, the system:
> - assigns an ID (ex: `DOC-2026-01-18-001`)
> - stores it in Supabase Storage
> - creates a DB record with metadata
> - adds it to a “Review Queue” if classification is incomplete
> 
> This is your executive-function crutch.
> 
> ## 2) Docket Library
> - Filter by date, phase, type
> - Preview PDFs in-browser
> - One tap: “Mark as Exhibit Candidate”
> - One tap: “Link to Violation”
> - One tap: “Add to Filing Packet”
> 
> ## 3) Motion Templates + Drafts
> Two buckets:
> - **Templates** (read-only)
> - **Drafts** (your working copies)
> 
> Flow you described:
> - Open template → Download to phone
> - Edit in Google Docs/Word
> - Export PDF
> - Upload back into Drafts
> - Mark as “Ready to File”
> - Attach exhibits from Docket Library
> 
> Important reality: editing `.docx` inside a web app on a phone is possible but usually painful. Don’t force it.
> Use **download-edit-upload** as your MVP.
> 
> ## 4) Filing Packets
> A Filing Packet is just:
> - Motion PDF (final)
> - Proposed order PDF (optional)
> - Exhibit list (auto-generated)
> - Attached exhibits (files)
> - Notes: where/how filed, confirmation number, date
> 
> Output:
> - One button: **Export Packet ZIP**
> - One button: **Export Exhibit List PDF** (optional)
> 
> ## 5) Ops Dashboard (“Next 5 Actions”)
> This is your “don’t get lost” page:
> - Current phase focus
> - Next 5 actions (P0/P1)
> - Waiting/blocked
> - Deadlines
> - Recent uploads
> 
> This replaces the brittle CSV approach.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Security that works on library computers
> This matters.
> 
> Minimum:
> - Supabase Auth with **magic link** + optional passcode
> - Short session duration
> - “Remember me” OFF by default
> - No sensitive data stored in LocalStorage beyond session token (or use in-memory)
> 
> Add-ons if you want hard mode:
> - Cloudflare Zero Trust in front of the app (private access)
> - Device posture checks (overkill for now)
> 
> ---
> 
> # Data model (minimal tables)
> This is enough to run everything above.
> 
> ### `documents`
> - `id` (generated)
> - `title`
> - `type` (docket/evidence/draft/template/media)
> - `phase` (01–06)
> - `source`
> - `storage_path`
> - `mime_type`
> - `uploaded_at`
> - `tags[]`
> - `linked_violation_ids[]` (optional)
> - `linked_filing_packet_id` (optional)
> 
> ### `templates`
> - `id`
> - `name`
> - `storage_path`
> - `version`
> - `notes`
> 
> ### `drafts`
> - `id`
> - `name`
> - `storage_path`
> - `status` (draft/ready/filed)
> - `related_packet_id`
> 
> ### `filing_packets`
> - `id`
> - `title`
> - `court`
> - `status` (building/ready/filed)
> - `filed_at`
> - `confirmation` (text)
> - `notes`
> 
> ### `tasks`
> - your normal tasks table (phase/status/priority/due)
> 
> You can add VIS later; don’t block MVP on it.
> 
> ---
> 
> # How this integrates with Quartz (without fragility)
> Quartz remains your read layer. The app links into Quartz, and Quartz links back to the app.
> 
> Later (optional):
> - A nightly job generates:
>   - `STATUS.md`
>   - `RESPONSE_TRACKING.md`
>   - “New uploads since last week”
> from Supabase → commits to repo → Quartz rebuild.
> 
> But **don’t require Quartz to operate the case**.
> The app must stand alone.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Deployment plan (fast, realistic)
> ## Phase 1 (MVP in days, not weeks)
> - Supabase project + RLS
> - Storage buckets: `docket`, `evidence`, `drafts`, `templates`
> - React PWA on Cloudflare Pages:
>   - Login
>   - Inbox Upload
>   - Documents list + preview
>   - Templates download
>   - Draft upload
>   - Tasks dashboard
> 
> ## Phase 2
> - Filing Packets + ZIP export
> - “Exhibit candidate” workflow
> - Simple “link doc to packet/violation”
> 
> ## Phase 3
> - Sync generated Quartz status pages
> - More automation (ID policies, exhibit list formatting)
> 
> ---
> 
> # The blunt truth about “full app”
> A “full app” can absolutely save you — but only if you keep it **narrow**:
> - Upload
> - Find
> - Draft
> - Packet
> - Next steps
> 
> If you start trying to re-create a legal practice management system, you’ll stall and the case will suffer.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Gemini build prompt (for the full app MVP)
> Paste this as-is:
> 
> ```text
> Build a minimal Case Ops web app (mobile-first PWA) for CASE_FCFCU.
> 
> Hosting:
> - Frontend: React + Vite deployed to Cloudflare Pages
> - Backend: Supabase (Postgres + Auth + Storage)
> - No separate always-on server. Use Supabase Edge Functions only if needed.
> 
> MVP user stories:
> 1) Login (magic link or password)
> 2) Inbox Upload:
>    - upload PDF/image/video
>    - choose type (docket/evidence/draft/template/media)
>    - choose phase (01-06)
>    - choose source (clerk/mycase/email/screenshot/other)
>    - save
>    - system assigns document_id and stores file to Supabase Storage and metadata to DB
> 3) Documents Library:
>    - list/filter by phase/type/date
>    - open/preview PDFs in browser
>    - copy share link (signed URL)
> 4) Templates:
>    - list templates
>    - download template to phone
> 5) Drafts:
>    - upload finished motion PDF
>    - status: draft/ready/filed
> 6) Dashboard:
>    - current phase focus
>    - next 5 tasks (P0/P1)
>    - blockers (waiting)
>    - recent uploads
> 
> Supabase:
> - Provide SQL to create tables:
>   documents, tasks, templates, drafts, filing_packets
> - Enable RLS:
>   allow authenticated user full CRUD
> - Storage buckets:
>   docket, evidence, drafts, templates, media
> - Use signed URLs for file access
> 
> Frontend:
> - Minimal UI, mobile-first
> - Use Supabase JS client
> - PWA manifest + service worker
> - Provide Cloudflare Pages build settings
> 
> Output:
> - SQL migration script
> - React project structure + core files
> - Deployment instructions for Cloudflare Pages
> - Environment variables list
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> ## One question I will NOT make you answer later
> Because you already answered it: you need continuity on phone/library PC. That means:
> 
> ### Do this now:
> - **Supabase + PWA**
> - Quartz remains read-only reference
> 
> If you want, next message I can give you:
> - the exact Supabase RLS policies (safe, not lock-you-out)
> - bucket rules
> - the folder naming policy for uploads so your evidence stays sane even in the app
> 
> Just say: **“Give me the Supabase SQL + RLS + bucket rules.”**

### User
> so before we do that we have to make sure that the phases have their sub phases or task lists, what goes with each, and the overal decision tree for what next depending on outcomes. mark whats done and whats pending what it relates to and honeslty draft wise we should already have the template inside the phase foldurs making it more modular so i also dont have to see unrelated templates and sucvh of ther phases confusign my mind. so like each phase should have the same sub folders. phase overview, phase related dockets or a link page to the docket docs, then phase templates for filings, motions, letters what have you, phase filings that are done and filed maybe a draft before hand, then something for how it inded or deciosn for whats next, im not sure maybe you understand what i am saying.

### Assistant
> You’re saying it clearly: you need **phase symmetry** plus a **decision tree** so you can operate the case on low executive function without wandering into the wrong lane.
> 
> Yes. Before we build the app, we lock the **phase operating system**:
> 
> 1) Each phase has the **same sub-structure**  
> 2) Each phase has a **task list** and **next-step decision tree**  
> 3) Templates live **inside the phase**, not globally  
> 4) Filings have **draft → filed → outcome → next** recorded in the same phase lane  
> 5) Cross-links exist, but the UI shows only the current lane by default
> 
> Below is the concrete structure to implement inside your existing repo.
> 
> ---
> 
> # 1) Phase Standard (Same subfolders in every phase)
> 
> Create these subfolders inside each phase folder under:
> 
> `content/10_PHASES/<PHASE_NAME>/`
> 
> ### Standard Subfolders (copy this across 01–06)
> ```text
> 00_PHASE_OVERVIEW/
> 10_TASKS_AND_STATUS/
> 20_DECISION_TREE/
> 30_DOCKET_LINKS/
> 40_TEMPLATES/
> 50_DRAFTS/
> 60_FILED/
> 70_OUTCOMES/
> 80_NOTES_INTERNAL/
> 90_EXPORTS/
> ```
> 
> ### What each folder is for (strict rules)
> - **00_PHASE_OVERVIEW/**  
>   One page: what this phase is, scope, objective, definition of “done.”
> 
> - **10_TASKS_AND_STATUS/**  
>   One page: task list + “done/pending” + links.
> 
> - **20_DECISION_TREE/**  
>   One page: “If X happens → do Y.” This is your anti-spiral map.
> 
> - **30_DOCKET_LINKS/**  
>   A link index page (not copies) pointing to relevant docket docs in Evidence Vault or Docket Library.
> 
> - **40_TEMPLATES/**  
>   Phase-specific templates only. No unrelated stuff.
> 
> - **50_DRAFTS/**  
>   Working drafts for this phase only.
> 
> - **60_FILED/**  
>   Final filed documents (PDF + the final MD text version if you want).
> 
> - **70_OUTCOMES/**  
>   Orders, responses, determinations, outcomes.
> 
> - **80_NOTES_INTERNAL/**  
>   Strategic notes, risk analysis, “what we believe vs can prove.”
> 
> - **90_EXPORTS/**  
>   Packets generated for filing (zip, combined PDFs, exhibit lists).
> 
> ---
> 
> # 2) Phase “Operating Pages” (same filenames in every phase)
> 
> Inside each phase, create these canonical files (so your app + scripts can rely on them):
> 
> ```text
> 00_PHASE_OVERVIEW/PHASE_OVERVIEW.md
> 10_TASKS_AND_STATUS/TASKS.md
> 20_DECISION_TREE/DECISION_TREE.md
> 30_DOCKET_LINKS/DOCKET_INDEX.md
> 40_TEMPLATES/README.md
> 60_FILED/FILED_INDEX.md
> 70_OUTCOMES/OUTCOMES_INDEX.md
> 80_NOTES_INTERNAL/NOTES.md
> ```
> 
> This gives you symmetry and predictable navigation.
> 
> ---
> 
> # 3) The “Decision Tree” format (simple, not fancy)
> 
> Each phase gets a single decision page like:
> 
> ## `20_DECISION_TREE/DECISION_TREE.md`
> ```markdown
> ---
> phase: "02"
> title: "Decision Tree — Credit Reporting (FCRA)"
> updated: 2026-01-18
> ---
> 
> # Entry Criteria (When we are in this phase)
> - Credit reporting harm exists (tradelines, missed payments, balance reporting)
> - Disputes pending or needed
> - Furnisher behavior inconsistent with satisfaction / court status
> 
> # Exit Criteria (Definition of Done)
> - Tradelines corrected OR deletion achieved OR written denial documented for litigation
> - Re-investigation results logged
> - Damages evidence captured (denials, rate impacts, screenshots)
> 
> # Decision Tree
> ## If the bureau deletes the tradeline
> → Mark phase tasks as DONE  
> → Move to Phase 05 (Litigation/Settlement) for damages demand if harm remains  
> → Archive communications in Evidence Vault
> 
> ## If the bureau "verifies" incorrectly
> → Send furnisher notice + method of verification request  
> → Escalate to CFPB/AG (Phase 04)  
> → Prepare FCRA claim packet (Phase 05)
> 
> ## If FCFCU continues reporting after satisfaction
> → Add violation entry in VIS  
> → Preserve screenshots + credit reports  
> → Demand letter packet (Phase 05)  
> → Regulatory complaint (Phase 04)
> 
> ## If we discover new tradeline/account or new furnisher
> → Add to tasks as P0  
> → Dispute immediately with all CRAs  
> → Request furnisher investigation details
> ```
> 
> That’s it. No overengineering.
> 
> ---
> 
> # 4) Your phases mapped to this structure (what each phase “means”)
> 
> You already have these phase roots:
> 
> - **01_Foreclosure_Core_Court_Record**
> - **02_credit_reporting_FCRA**
> - **03_ownership_obligations_purge**
> - **04_regulations_civil_rights**
> - **05_litigation_settlement**
> - **06_Public_Accountability**
> 
> Here’s the clean “purpose + outputs” for each:
> 
> ## Phase 01 — Foreclosure Core / Court Record
> **Goal:** jurisdiction, service, orders, writ, removal chain.  
> **Outputs:** motion(s), proposed orders, exhibit sets, hearing packet.
> 
> ## Phase 02 — Credit Reporting (FCRA)
> **Goal:** stop reporting harm, correct/delete tradelines, capture damages trail.  
> **Outputs:** bureau disputes, furnisher notice, verification challenges, complaint packet.
> 
> ## Phase 03 — Ownership Obligations & Purge
> **Goal:** force utilities/HOA/city to reverse charges after transfer date; stop collections.  
> **Outputs:** notices, account correction requests, disputes, proof packet.
> 
> ## Phase 04 — Regulators & Civil Rights
> **Goal:** parallel pressure + accommodations compliance + agency record creation.  
> **Outputs:** AG, Civil Rights, DOJ ADA, CFPB (if used), response tracking.
> 
> ## Phase 05 — Litigation & Settlement
> **Goal:** demand package + negotiation + suit readiness if they refuse.  
> **Outputs:** damages model, demand letter(s), draft complaint(s), settlement terms.
> 
> ## Phase 06 — Public Accountability
> **Goal:** public narrative and pattern dossier (only when safe).  
> **Outputs:** sanitized story, timeline, exhibits curated for public.
> 
> ---
> 
> # 5) “Modular templates per phase” (your key requirement)
>

> - `TEMPLATE_letter_...`
> - `TEMPLATE_motion_...`
> - `TEMPLATE_notice_...`
> - `TEMPLATE_packet_cover_...`
> 
> And a `README.md` that says:
> - what the template is for
> - when to use it
> - what evidence IDs to attach
> - where it gets filed (MyCase, email, certified mail, etc.)
> 
> This prevents the “unrelated templates” cognitive mess.
>

> - Top objective

> - Completed items

> ## Waiting / Blocked
> - [ ] …
> ## Done
> - [x] …
> ## Key Links
> - Filed index: ../60_FILED/FILED_INDEX.md
> - Outcomes: ../70_OUTCOMES/OUTCOMES_INDEX.md
> - Docket links: ../30_DOCKET_LINKS/DOCKET_INDEX.md
> ```
> 
> This page is what your future app reads and shows as the phase dashboard if you want.

### User
> unless we keep it mono repo but create views somehow in the app what is faster to mvp?

### Assistant
> Keep it **mono repo**. Create **views in the app**. That is faster to MVP and safer long-term.
> 
> Splitting repos/folders to match “views” feels tidy, but it slows you down immediately:
> - more wiring
> - more sync problems
> - more “where did I put that file”
> - more chances to break evidence integrity
> 
> Mono repo + database-driven views is the correct split:
> - **Repo = record (files)**
> - **App = views + workflow (database)**
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Fastest MVP path (realistic, minimal moving parts)
> 
> ### What stays in the repo (unchanged)
> - `content/` = Quartz view + evidence vault + drafts + exports
> - Your standardized phase folders and templates remain file-based
> 
> ### What goes in Supabase (live “ops state”)
> - tasks (phase/status/priority)
> - documents index (metadata + storage pointers)
> - filing packets index
> - complaints/responses
> 
> ### What the app does (views)
> - “Current Phase” view (filters tasks + docs)
> - “Next 5 actions” view
> - “Upload docket doc” view
> - “Templates by phase” view (only show templates for current phase)
> - “Packet builder” view (select doc IDs and export a zip later)
> 
> You don’t need to restructure the repo to get clarity; you need the UI to **hide irrelevant stuff**.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## MVP scope decision: 2 viable tracks
> 
> ### Track A (fastest to ship): Supabase Studio + thin Quartz
> **Time-to-working:** fastest  
> **UI quality:** acceptable  
> **Complexity:** low  
> **Best if:** you need “live now” and can tolerate a basic UI.
> 
> - Use Supabase Studio on your phone as the “case manager”
> - Use Quartz as read/search/browse
> - Use one sync script later (optional)
> 
> This gets you operational without building anything.
> 
> ### Track B (still fast, better UX): React PWA on Cloudflare + Supabase
> **Time-to-working:** still MVP-friendly  
> **UI quality:** good  
> **Complexity:** moderate  
> **Best if:** you need the UX to prevent mistakes.
> 
> This is what you said you want.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## The fastest MVP for Track B (what I’d build first)
> To be clear: **do not** start with packet export or fancy automation.
> 
> ### MVP screens (only 4)
> 1) **Login**
> 2) **Dashboard**  
>    - Current phase selector  
>    - Next 5 actions  
>    - Waiting/blocked
> 3) **Inbox Upload**  
>    - upload → tag phase/type/source → save
> 4) **Phase View**  
>    - shows only: phase tasks + phase templates + recent docs
> 
> That’s enough to keep the case alive from a phone.
> 
> Everything else can come next.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Mono repo vs multi repo: why mono wins for you
> - You’re already running Quartz against `content/`
> - Your evidence integrity model depends on consistent paths
> - You’re frequently on unstable hardware; fewer moving parts wins
> - “Views” are a UI concern, not a filesystem concern
> 
> So: **mono repo, strict folder symmetry, UI views by phase.**
> 
> ---
>

> 1) Implement the **phase standard subfolders** (symmetry) inside each phase (we already defined it).  
> 2) Create Supabase tables:
>    - `tasks`
>    - `documents`
>    - `templates`
>    - `drafts`
>    - `filing_packets`
> 3) Build the React PWA MVP screens above.
> 4) Later: add sync/export automation.

### User
> shouldnt the tables be tasks, documents, templates, drafts, packets, then don't we need linking tablet for filing envelopes when efiled, and phases to connect the tables to a phase, what about the printable packet copies for judge and ops counsel. i want number 2,

### Assistant
> Yes — your instincts are correct. For option **#2 (React PWA + Supabase)** you want a schema that supports:
> 
> - Phase-scoped work (so the UI can hide irrelevant stuff)
> - Filing “envelopes” (e-file submissions) that group packets + metadata
> - Packet exports for **judge copies / opposing counsel / service** as distinct artifacts
> - Many-to-many links (docs ↔ packets, packets ↔ envelopes, tasks ↔ phases, etc.)
> 
> You do **not** need to overcomplicate it. You need **one anchor table** (`phases`) and then link everything to it with FKs plus a couple junction tables.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 1) Minimal-but-correct table set (MVP+)
> 
> ### Core tables (what you listed)
> 1) `phases`
> 2) `tasks`
> 3) `documents`
> 4) `templates`
> 5) `drafts`
> 6) `packets`
> 
> ### Required linking tables (you called this)
> 7) `packet_items` (documents/drafts/templates included in a packet)
> 8) `envelopes` (efile submissions)
> 9) `envelope_packets` (many packets per envelope)
> 10) `packet_exports` (printable builds / service sets / judge copies)
> 
> That’s the clean MVP that won’t paint you into a corner.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 2) What each table does (no fluff)
> 
> ### `phases`
> Defines the 01–06 lanes and lets the app filter everything.
> - `id` = `'01'..'06'`
> - `name`
> - `status` (active/hold/done)
> - `current_focus` (text)
> 
> ### `tasks`
> Your live operating system.
> - `phase_id` FK → `phases.id`
> - `status`, `priority`, `due_date`
> - optional: `related_packet_id`, `related_doc_id`
> 
> ### `documents`
> Any uploaded file: docket PDFs, photos, receipts, court orders, screenshots.
> - `phase_id`
> - `type` (docket/evidence/order/correspondence/media/etc.)
> - `storage_bucket`, `storage_path`
> - `source` (MyCase/Clerk/Email/etc.)
> - tags + linkable fields
> 
> ### `templates`
> Phase-scoped templates only.
> - `phase_id`
> - `template_type` (motion/letter/notice/order/etc.)
> - stored in Storage under `templates/`
> 
> ### `drafts`
> Working documents you’re iterating.
> - `phase_id`
> - `draft_type` (motion/proposed_order/letter/etc.)
> - `status` (draft/ready/filed)
> - stored in `drafts/`
> 
> ### `packets`
> A “packet” is what you assemble for a purpose.
> Examples:
> - “Emergency Motion to Stay + Exhibits”
> - “Credit Bureau Dispute Packet - Experian”
> - “Judge courtesy copy set”
> - “Opposing counsel service set”
> 
> Fields:
> - `phase_id`
> - `packet_type` (efile / judge_copy / service / dispute / regulator)
> - `status` (building/ready/submitted/sent)
> 
> ### `packet_items` (junction)
> Links packet ↔ items.
> - `packet_id`
> - `item_type` (`document` | `draft` | `template`)
> - `item_id`
> - `order_index`
> - `notes`
> This gives you modular packet composition.
> 
> ### `envelopes`
> Represents an actual e-file submission event.
> - `phase_id`
> - `court_system` (MyCase / Odyssey / etc.)
> - `submitted_at`
> - `confirmation_number`
> - `status` (draft/submitted/accepted/rejected)
> - `rejection_reason`
> - `notes`
> 
> ### `envelope_packets` (junction)
> Because one envelope might include multiple packets or subcomponents.
> - `envelope_id`
> - `packet_id`
> 
> ### `packet_exports`
> Tracks printable/exported builds:
> - `packet_id`
> - `export_type` (`judge_copy` | `opposing_counsel` | `service` | `internal`)
> - `format` (`pdf` | `zip`)
> - `storage_path` (in `exports/`)
> - `created_at`
> This is where your “print 2 copies for judge” reality lives.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 3) Do we need a separate “filing copies” table?
> Not necessarily. `packet_exports` covers:
> - judge copy PDF
> - opposing counsel PDF
> - service set ZIP
> - print-ready binder PDF
> 
> If later you want detailed print logistics, add `print_jobs`. Not in MVP.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 4) How the app uses this to prevent confusion
> - App shows **Current Phase** selector at the top.
> - Every screen defaults to `phase_id = current`.
> - Templates list is filtered by phase.
> - Packets list is filtered by phase.
> - Upload form forces selecting phase (or uses current by default).
> This is how you stop your brain from seeing everything at once.
> 
> ---
> 
> # 5) GEMINI PROMPT (Option #2) — build Supabase + React PWA with phase views + envelopes + exports
> Paste this exactly:
> 
> ```text
> You are a senior full-stack engineer. Build a minimal Case Ops PWA for CASE_FCFCU that works on mobile and library computers.
> 
> Hosting:
> - Frontend: React + Vite deployed to Cloudflare Pages
> - Backend: Supabase (Postgres + Auth + Storage)
> - No always-on custom server. Use Supabase Edge Functions only if needed.
> 
> Core requirement:
> Everything is phase-scoped. The UI defaults to the current phase and hides unrelated templates/docs.
> 
> Supabase tables (create with SQL migration):
> 1) phases:
> - id text primary key check in ('01','02','03','04','05','06')
> - name text not null
> - status text not null check in ('active','hold','done') default 'active'
> - current_focus text null
> - created_at timestamptz default now()
> - updated_at timestamptz default now()
> 
> 2) tasks:
> - id uuid pk default gen_random_uuid()
> - phase_id text not null references phases(id)
> - title text not null
> - status text not null check in ('todo','doing','waiting','done')
> - priority text not null check in ('P0','P1','P2','P3')
> - due_date date null
> - links jsonb null
> - notes text null
> - related_packet_id uuid null
> - related_document_id uuid null
> - created_at timestamptz default now()
> - updated_at timestamptz default now()
> 
> 3) documents:
> - id uuid pk default gen_random_uuid()
> - phase_id text not null references phases(id)
> - title text not null
> - doc_type text not null (e.g. docket,evidence,order,correspondence,media)
> - source text null
> - storage_bucket text not null
> - storage_path text not null
> - mime_type text null
> - tags text[] default '{}'
> - occurred_at date null
> - created_at timestamptz default now()
> - updated_at timestamptz default now()
> 
> 4) templates:
> - id uuid pk default gen_random_uuid()
> - phase_id text not null references phases(id)
> - name text not null
> - template_type text not null (motion, letter, notice, proposed_order, packet_cover)
> - storage_bucket text not null
> - storage_path text not null
> - version text null
> - notes text null
> - created_at timestamptz default now()
> - updated_at timestamptz default now()
> 
> 5) drafts:
> - id uuid pk default gen_random_uuid()
> - phase_id text not null references phases(id)
> - name text not null
> - draft_type text not null (motion, proposed_order, letter, exhibit_list)
> - status text not null check in ('draft','ready','filed') default 'draft'
> - storage_bucket text not null
> - storage_path text not null
> - notes text null
> - created_at timestamptz default now()
> - updated_at timestamptz default now()
> 
> 6) packets:
> - id uuid pk default gen_random_uuid()
> - phase_id text not null references phases(id)
> - title text not null
> - packet_type text not null check in ('efile','judge_copy','service','dispute','regulator','internal')
> - status text not null check in ('building','ready','submitted','sent') default 'building'
> - notes text null
> - created_at timestamptz default now()
> - updated_at timestamptz default now()
> 
> 7) packet_items (junction):
> - id uuid pk default gen_random_uuid()
> - packet_id uuid not null references packets(id) on delete cascade
> - item_type text not null check in ('document','draft','template')
> - item_id uuid not null
> - order_index int not null default 0
> - notes text null
> - created_at timestamptz default now()
> 
> 8) envelopes (efile submissions):
> - id uuid pk default gen_random_uuid()
> - phase_id text not null references phases(id)
> - court_system text not null
> - status text not null check in ('draft','submitted','accepted','rejected') default 'draft'
> - submitted_at timestamptz null
> - confirmation_number text null
> - rejection_reason text null
> - notes text null
> - created_at timestamptz default now()
> - updated_at timestamptz default now()
> 
> 9) envelope_packets (junction):
> - id uuid pk default gen_random_uuid()
> - envelope_id uuid not null references envelopes(id) on delete cascade
> - packet_id uuid not null references packets(id) on delete cascade
> - created_at timestamptz default now()
> 
> 10) packet_exports:
> - id uuid pk default gen_random_uuid()
> - packet_id uuid not null references packets(id) on delete cascade
> - export_type text not null check in ('judge_copy','opposing_counsel','service','internal')
> - format text not null check in ('pdf','zip')
> - storage_bucket text not null
> - storage_path text not null
> - created_at timestamptz default now()
> 
> Also:
> - Add updated_at triggers for all tables.
> - Enable RLS and add policies so authenticated users have full CRUD.
> - Create storage buckets: documents, templates, drafts, exports
> - Storage access: authenticated only + signed URLs for viewing/downloading.
> 
> Frontend PWA (React + Vite):
> Pages:
> 1) Login
> 2) Dashboard:
>    - current phase selector (persists)
>    - Next 5 tasks (P0/P1 todo/doing)
>    - Waiting/blockers
>    - Recent uploads
> 3) Inbox Upload:
>    - upload file
>    - choose doc_type and source (defaults)
>    - phase defaults to current phase
>    - save metadata + upload to Storage
> 4) Phase View:
>    - tabs: Tasks, Documents, Templates, Drafts, Packets
>    - everything filtered by phase
> 5) Packet Builder:
>    - create packet (type/title)
>    - add items from documents/drafts/templates
>    - reorder items
> 6) Envelopes:
>    - create envelope, attach packets
>    - record submission confirmation, acceptance/rejection
> 7) Exports:
>    - list packet_exports
>    - upload export PDF/ZIP (manual for MVP)
> 
> Notes:
> - For MVP, do not implement server-side PDF merging. Exports can be uploaded manually.
> - Provide Cloudflare Pages build settings.
> - Provide environment variables: VITE_SUPABASE_URL, VITE_SUPABASE_ANON_KEY
> 
> Output:
> - SQL migration
> - RLS policies
> - Storage bucket rules
> - React project file tree + core code
> - Deployment instructions
> ```

### User
> so we dont use render.com full stack hobby plan

### Assistant
> Correct. **Do not use Render.com’s full-stack hobby plan** for this project.
> 
> Here’s the straight, no-nonsense rationale tied to your actual constraints (phone-first, continuity, legal integrity, low executive function, zero surprise billing).
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Why Render.com is the wrong tool *for this case*
> 
> ### 1. You don’t actually need a traditional backend server
> What people use Render/Fly/Railway for:
> - Long-running APIs
> - WebSockets
> - Custom server logic
> - Heavy background jobs
> 
> What **your case system needs**:
> - Auth
> - CRUD on structured data
> - File storage
> - Signed URLs
> - Occasional automation (exports, sync)
> 
> Supabase already provides all of that **without** you managing a server.
> 
> Adding Render would just give you:
> - Another failure point
> - Another bill
> - Another place things can break when your laptop dies
> 
> ---
> 
> ### 2. Render free/hobby plans are fragile by design
> Render free services:
> - Sleep
> - Have cold starts
> - Have compute limits
> - Are not meant to be relied on in high-pressure, time-sensitive workflows
> 
> That’s fine for demos.  
> It is **not** fine when you’re filing motions, uploading dockets, or racing deadlines.
> 
> You already know what happens when infra flakes out at the wrong moment.
> 
> ---
> 
> ### 3. Mobile + library-computer use makes servers a liability
> If you’re on:
> - a phone
> - a public computer
> - an unreliable Chromebook
> 
> You want:
> - zero local setup
> - zero SSH
> - zero server restarts
> - zero “deploy failed” mysteries
> 
> Supabase + Cloudflare Pages = browser only.
> 
> Render = “why is my service sleeping?” at exactly the wrong time.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## The correct split (final answer)
> 
> ### What you **do** use
> - **Supabase**  
>   - Database  
>   - Auth  
>   - Storage  
>   - Edge Functions (optional, later)
> 
> - **Cloudflare Pages**  
>   - React PWA (case ops app)  
>   - Quartz (read/search/browse)
> 
> - **GitHub**  
>   - Mono-repo source of truth  
>   - Versioning  
>   - Optional scheduled jobs
> 
> ### What you **do not** use
> - Render
> - Fly.io
> - Railway
> - Dedicated VM
> - Self-hosted backend
> 
> Not for MVP. Not for this use case.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## If (later) you *ever* need a backend server
> Only consider it if you need:

> # One more thing: your schema needs a `user_id` column
> If you don’t include `user_id` on each table, your RLS either becomes:
> - wide open, or
> - painful to manage
> 
> So when Gemini generates SQL, it must add:
> - `user_id uuid not null default auth.uid()` for user-owned tables
> and RLS policies like:
> - `using (user_id = auth.uid())`
> 
> **Exception:** `phases` can be global/seeded. Everything else should be user-scoped.
> 
> Tell Gemini explicitly if you are a single-user system; still keep `user_id` because it prevents accidental data leakage and makes policies trivial.
> 
> ---
>

> Magic link login or password login?
> 
> If you’re often on library machines: **magic link** is safer (no password typed on public PCs).  
> If you need speed offline-ish: password.
> 
> If you don’t answer, I’ll default to **magic link**, because it’s the least risky on shared computers.

### Assistant
> Correct — and you’re 100% right to call this out now.
> 
> Gemini (and most LLMs) **will not reliably produce a large, multi-artifact system in one pass**, even with a manifest requirement. Trying to force it all at once is exactly why you got the glossy “proposal” instead of working files.
> 
> So the right move is to **turn this into a staged build with hard checkpoints**, where each step produces *one class of artifacts*, you validate them, then move to the next step.
> 
> Below is the **exact staged plan + the exact prompts** you should use, in order. This keeps control in your hands and prevents drift.
> 
> ---
> 
> # THE RULE (lock this in mentally)
> 
> **One prompt = one artifact family.**  
> If a prompt asks for:
> - schema + frontend + manifest + PWA → it will fail.
> 
> Instead:
> - Schema first
> - Then RLS
> - Then storage
> - Then frontend skeleton
> - Then pages
> - Then wiring
> - Then polish
> 
> ---
> 
> # STAGED BUILD PLAN (what we’re doing)
> 
> We will build this app in **7 stages**. Each stage is *independently usable* and does not depend on Gemini remembering earlier context.
> 
> You will **paste outputs into your repo as you go**.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## STAGE 1 — DATABASE SCHEMA ONLY (NO FRONTEND)
> 
> ### Goal
> Get a **correct, stable Supabase schema** that:
> - matches your phase logic
> - supports packets, envelopes, exports
> - includes `user_id`
> - has no RLS yet (so we don’t lock ourselves out)
> 
> ### Gemini Prompt #1 (copy/paste exactly)
> 
> ```text
> You are generating ONLY a Supabase SQL schema.
> 
> Scope:
> - Database schema ONLY
> - No frontend
> - No RLS
> - No storage policies
> - No explanations
> 
> Output requirements:
> - Output a single SQL file named: supabase/migrations/0001_init.sql
> - Include FULL SQL contents
> - Use PostgreSQL syntax compatible with Supabase
> 
> Tables to create:
> - phases
> - tasks
> - documents
> - templates
> - drafts
> - packets
> - packet_items
> - envelopes
> - envelope_packets
> - packet_exports
> 
> Rules:
> 1) Every table except `phases` MUST include:
>    user_id uuid not null default auth.uid()
> 2) All tables must include:
>    created_at timestamptz default now()
>    updated_at timestamptz default now()
> 3) Use appropriate foreign keys.
> 4) `phases.id` must be text ('01'..'06').
> 5) Do NOT include RLS.
> 6) Do NOT include triggers yet.
> 7) Do NOT include storage.
> 8) Do NOT include sample data.
> 
> Output format:
> - One fenced SQL code block only.
> - No commentary.
> ```
> 
> **You do not proceed until this SQL looks correct.**
>

> - phases table:
>   - readable by all authenticated users
>   - writable by authenticated users (single-user system)
>

> - One fenced SQL code block only.
> ```
>

### User
> give me a script to create the directory of this app with the files to so i can just copy and passte in the code from gemini as he give it to me.

### Assistant
> Good call. This is exactly how you keep control while letting Gemini generate code piece-by-piece.
> 
> Below is a **single, safe, copy-pasteable setup script** that:
> 
> - Creates the **entire app directory tree**
> - Creates **empty placeholder files** with correct names
> - Does **not** overwrite existing files
> - Lets you paste Gemini’s output file-by-file without confusion
> - Works on **Mac, Linux, Chromebook, Codespaces**, and most shells
> 
> You run this **once**, then only paste content into files Gemini generates.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## ✅ RECOMMENDED: Bash script (works everywhere)
> 
> Create a file called:
> 
> ```text
> init_case_ops_app.sh
> ```
> 
> Paste this entire script into it:
> 
> ```bash
> #!/usr/bin/env bash
> set -e
> 
> APP_ROOT="case-ops"
> 
> echo "Creating Case Ops app structure at ./$APP_ROOT"
> 
> # --- Root ---
> mkdir -p "$APP_ROOT"
> cd "$APP_ROOT"
> 
> # --- Supabase ---
> mkdir -p supabase/migrations
> touch supabase/migrations/0001_init.sql
> touch supabase/migrations/0002_updated_at_triggers.sql
> touch supabase/migrations/0003_rls.sql
> touch supabase/migrations/0004_storage.sql
> 
> # --- Public / PWA ---
> mkdir -p public/icons
> touch public/manifest.webmanifest
> touch public/icons/icon-192.svg
> touch public/icons/icon-512.svg
> 
> # --- Source ---
> mkdir -p src/{components,pages,lib}

> ## While Copilot is reviewing: what you should be checking (quick checklist)
> 
> ### 1) **File placement discipline**
> Copilot loves to:
> - merge files
> - suggest renames
> - “simplify” structure
> 
> **Reject immediately** if it suggests:
> - collapsing files into `App.tsx`
> - moving Supabase logic into components
> - inventing new folders not in your tree
> - renaming migration files
> 
> Rule:  
> **If it’s not already in the tree, it doesn’t exist.**
> 
> ---
> 
> ### 2) **Supabase client usage**
> Copilot often:
> - hardcodes Supabase keys
> - instantiates multiple clients
> - puts client code in components
> 
> You want:
> - exactly **one** Supabase client in  
>   `src/lib/supabase.ts`
> - imported everywhere else
> 
> Red flags:
> - `createClient` appearing anywhere else
> - keys referenced outside env vars
> 
> ---
> 
> ### 3) **Auth flow sanity**
> Given your constraints (library computers):
> 
> Correct:
> - magic link login
> - session stored in memory / Supabase
> - no custom password handling
> 
> Reject if Copilot:
> - adds password reset flows
> - stores tokens manually
> - adds “remember me” logic
> 
> You want boring and safe.
> 
> ---
> 
> ### 4) **Phase scoping**
> Copilot may ignore your phase discipline.
> 
> Every query should:
> - either explicitly filter by `phase_id`
> - or use the “current phase” context from `phase.ts`
> 
> If you see:
> ```ts
> .from('documents').select('*')
> ```
> with no phase filter — that’s a bug.
> 
> ---
> 
> ### 5) **User scoping**
> Every insert/select/update must be scoped to `user_id = auth.uid()` implicitly via RLS.
> 
> If Copilot tries to:
> - manually pass `user_id`
> - or ignore user scoping entirely
> 
> That’s fine **only if RLS is correct**, but watch for:
> - policies missing `using (user_id = auth.uid())`
> 
> ---
> 
> ## What NOT to do while Copilot is reviewing
> - Don’t “fix” things preemptively.
> - Don’t accept large refactors.
> - Don’t let it rewrite your schema.
> 
> You’re evaluating correctness, not speed.

> 
> Supabase confirms using `auth.uid()` inside policies is the correct pattern, and they recommend separate policies per operation (select/insert/update/delete). citeturn0search1turn0search9
>

> Supabase Storage access is controlled via RLS policies on `storage.objects`. By default, uploads are blocked until you add policies. citeturn0search0turn0search4  
> And yes: your policies target `storage.objects`, not bucket rows. citeturn0search16

>   ('06','Public Accountability','hold',null)

> ```

> -- Enable UUID extension if not already enabled

> CREATE EXTENSION IF NOT EXISTS "uuid-ossp";

> 

> -- 1. phases table (No user_id constraint)

> CREATE TABLE phases (

>     id text PRIMARY KEY, -- '01', '02', etc.

>     name text NOT NULL,

>     description text,

>     created_at timestamptz DEFAULT now(),

>     updated_at timestamptz DEFAULT now()

> );

> 

> -- 2. tasks table

> CREATE TABLE tasks (

>     id uuid PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT uuid_generate_v4(),

>     user_id uuid NOT NULL DEFAULT auth.uid(),

>     phase_id text REFERENCES phases(id) ON DELETE CASCADE,

>     title text NOT NULL,

>     description text,

>     status text DEFAULT 'pending',

>     due_date timestamptz,

>     created_at timestamptz DEFAULT now(),

>     updated_at timestamptz DEFAULT now()

> );

> 

> -- 3. documents table

> CREATE TABLE documents (

>     id uuid PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT uuid_generate_v4(),

>     user_id uuid NOT NULL DEFAULT auth.uid(),

>     task_id uuid REFERENCES tasks(id) ON DELETE SET NULL,

>     title text NOT NULL,

>     file_path text,

>     file_type text,

>     size_bytes bigint,

>     metadata jsonb DEFAULT '{}'::jsonb,

>     created_at timestamptz DEFAULT now(),

>     updated_at timestamptz DEFAULT now()

> );

> 

> -- 4. templates table

> CREATE TABLE templates (

>     id uuid PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT uuid_generate_v4(),

>     user_id uuid NOT NULL DEFAULT auth.uid(),

>     name text NOT NULL,

>     content text,

>     category text,

>     is_active boolean DEFAULT true,

>     created_at timestamptz DEFAULT now(),

>     updated_at timestamptz DEFAULT now()

> );

> 

> -- 5. drafts table

> CREATE TABLE drafts (

>     id uuid PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT uuid_generate_v4(),

>     user_id uuid NOT NULL DEFAULT auth.uid(),

>     template_id uuid REFERENCES templates(id) ON DELETE SET NULL,

>     title text,

>     content_data jsonb DEFAULT '{}'::jsonb,

>     status text DEFAULT 'draft',

>     created_at timestamptz DEFAULT now(),

>     updated_at timestamptz DEFAULT now()

> );

> 

> -- 6. packets table

> CREATE TABLE packets (

>     id uuid PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT uuid_generate_v4(),

>     user_id uuid NOT NULL DEFAULT auth.uid(),

>     name text NOT NULL,

>     description text,

>     status text DEFAULT 'open',

>     version integer DEFAULT 1,

>     created_at timestamptz DEFAULT now(),

>     updated_at timestamptz DEFAULT now()

> );

> 

> -- 7. packet_items table

> CREATE TABLE packet_items (

>     id uuid PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT uuid_generate_v4(),

>     user_id uuid NOT NULL DEFAULT auth.uid(),

>     packet_id uuid REFERENCES packets(id) ON DELETE CASCADE,

>     document_id uuid REFERENCES documents(id) ON DELETE CASCADE,

>     draft_id uuid REFERENCES drafts(id) ON DELETE SET NULL,

>     sort_order integer DEFAULT 0,

>     created_at timestamptz DEFAULT now(),

>     updated_at timestamptz DEFAULT now()

> );

> 

> -- 8. envelopes table

> CREATE TABLE envelopes (

>     id uuid PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT uuid_generate_v4(),

>     user_id uuid NOT NULL DEFAULT auth.uid(),

>     recipient_email text,

>     recipient_name text,

>     status text DEFAULT 'prepared',

>     sent_at timestamptz,

>     created_at timestamptz DEFAULT now(),

>     updated_at timestamptz DEFAULT now()

> );

> 

> -- 9. envelope_packets table

> CREATE TABLE envelope_packets (

>     id uuid PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT uuid_generate_v4(),

>     user_id uuid NOT NULL DEFAULT auth.uid(),

>     envelope_id uuid REFERENCES envelopes(id) ON DELETE CASCADE,

>     packet_id uuid REFERENCES packets(id) ON DELETE CASCADE,

>     created_at timestamptz DEFAULT now(),

>     updated_at timestamptz DEFAULT now()

> );

> 

> -- 10. packet_exports table

> CREATE TABLE packet_exports (

>     id uuid PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT uuid_generate_v4(),

>     user_id uuid NOT NULL DEFAULT auth.uid(),

>     packet_id uuid REFERENCES packets(id) ON DELETE CASCADE,

>     export_url text,

>     format text DEFAULT 'pdf',

>     status text DEFAULT 'processing',

>     completed_at timestamptz,

>     created_at timestamptz DEFAULT now(),

>     updated_at timestamptz DEFAULT now()

> );

### Assistant
> Good — this is enough to audit `0001_init.sql`. Bluntly: it’s a **usable starting point**, but it has a few structural problems that will bite you fast (especially phase-scoping and packet composition), and a couple of tech choices I’d change immediately.
> 
> ## What’s good
> - `user_id uuid default auth.uid()` on user-owned tables: correct.
> - `phases` global: fine.
> - Separation of packets/envelopes/exports: correct direction.
> - JSONB fields where flexibility helps (`metadata`, `content_data`): fine.
> 
> ## What will fall apart (and how to fix it)
> 
> ### 1) `tasks.status` is unconstrained and mismatched to your model
> You used `status text default 'pending'`. You want a small controlled set for UI + decision trees.
> 
> **Fix:** Add CHECK constraints and add `priority`.
> ```sql
> status text not null default 'todo' check (status in ('todo','doing','waiting','done')),
> priority text not null default 'P2' check (priority in ('P0','P1','P2','P3')),
> ```
> 
> ### 2) `phase_id` on tasks should be NOT NULL and restricted
> Right now tasks can exist without a phase, and phase IDs aren’t limited to `'01'..'06'`.
> 
> **Fix:**
> - In `phases`: enforce allowed IDs.
> - In `tasks`: `phase_id text not null references phases(id)`.
> 
> In `phases` table:
> ```sql
> id text primary key check (id in ('01','02','03','04','05','06')),
> ```
> 
> ### 3) Documents are tied to `task_id` instead of `phase_id` (bad for filtering)
> This will break the “phase view” concept. Documents need to be phase-scoped directly (tasks are optional associations).
> 
> **Fix:** Add `phase_id` to `documents` (NOT NULL) and keep `task_id` optional.
> ```sql
> phase_id text not null references phases(id) on delete restrict,
> task_id uuid references tasks(id) on delete set null,
> ```
> 
> Also: `file_path` should be `storage_bucket` + `storage_path` (so you can use Supabase Storage cleanly), not one string.
> 
> ### 4) Templates are not phase-scoped (this violates your cognitive rule)
> You explicitly said templates must be inside each phase and the UI must not show unrelated templates.
> 
> **Fix:** add `phase_id` to `templates` and `drafts`.
> ```sql
> templates.phase_id text not null references phases(id),
> drafts.phase_id text not null references phases(id),
> ```
> 
> ### 5) Packet composition is ambiguous and will cause duplicates / confusion
> `packet_items` has both `document_id` and `draft_id`, both nullable, and no rule that exactly one is set. This is a classic integrity bug.
> 
> **Fix (cleanest):** Use `item_type` + `item_id` (single polymorphic reference), OR enforce XOR constraints.
> 
> Since Postgres can’t FK a polymorphic ID cleanly, the pragmatic MVP approach is **XOR constraint** with your current columns:
> 
> ```sql
> -- ensure exactly one of document_id or draft_id is set
> check (
>   (document_id is not null and draft_id is null)
>   or
>   (document_id is null and draft_id is not null)
> ),
> ```
> 
> Also add `order_index` NOT NULL.
> 
> ### 6) Envelopes currently look like “email envelopes,” not “efile submissions”
> You want e-file envelopes (MyCase/Odyssey) with confirmation numbers, acceptance/rejection, etc. Right now it’s recipient email/name.
> 
> **Fix:** Replace envelope fields with:
> - `phase_id`
> - `court_system`
> - `status` (draft/submitted/accepted/rejected)
> - `submitted_at`
> - `confirmation_number`
> - `rejection_reason`
> - `notes`
> 
> Keep recipient fields *later* if you add service mailers.
> 
> ### 7) Using `uuid-ossp` is fine, but `pgcrypto` is more standard now
> Supabase commonly uses `gen_random_uuid()` from `pgcrypto`. `uuid-ossp` works, but I’d switch.
> 
> **Fix:**
> ```sql
> create extension if not exists pgcrypto;
> id uuid primary key default gen_random_uuid()
> ```
> 
> ### 8) Missing indexes you will need for performance
> Not urgent for MVP, but low cost to add now:
> - `tasks(user_id, phase_id, status)`
> - `documents(user_id, phase_id)`
> - `packet_items(packet_id, sort_order)`
> - `envelope_packets(envelope_id)`
> 
> ---
> 
> # Recommended “v2” schema changes (minimal diffs)
> If you haven’t run this yet, adjust it before you do. If you already ran it, we can do `ALTER TABLE` migrations.
> 
> Here is the **exact change list** you want Gemini to produce next as `0001_init.sql` (or as `0001b_patch.sql` if already applied):
> 
> ### Must-add columns/constraints
> - `phases.id` CHECK to only allow 01–06
> - `tasks.phase_id` NOT NULL, add `priority` and constrained `status`
> - `documents.phase_id` NOT NULL and storage fields
> - `templates.phase_id` NOT NULL
> - `drafts.phase_id` NOT NULL
> - `packets.phase_id` NOT NULL and `packet_type` + constrained `status`
> - `packet_items` XOR constraint
> - rework `envelopes` to be efile submission tracking
> 
> ---
> 
> # What I need next to finish the safety audit
> Paste your other three files (`0002`, `0003`, `0004`) the same way you pasted `0001`.
> 
> Specifically, I’m looking for:
> - `updated_at` trigger function correctness
> - RLS policies that **won’t lock you out** (common failure)
> - storage bucket + `storage.objects` policies that actually allow upload/read
> 
> ## Do not run 0003 or 0004 until I review them.
> Because a bad storage policy = “uploads fail on phone” and a bad RLS = “everything looks empty and you panic.”
> 
> ---
> 
> # If you want the next prompt for Gemini (schema patch only)
> Here’s the tight “patch generation” prompt you can feed Gemini:
> 
> ```text
> Generate a Supabase SQL migration file to PATCH an existing schema.
> 
> Input: current tables phases, tasks, documents, templates, drafts, packets, packet_items, envelopes, envelope_packets, packet_exports.
> 
> Output: a single SQL migration file named supabase/migrations/0001b_patch_schema.sql that:
> 1) switches uuid generation to pgcrypto gen_random_uuid() where safe (do not drop columns)
> 2) enforces phases.id check constraint to only allow '01'..'06'
> 3) updates tasks:
>    - phase_id set NOT NULL
>    - status check in ('todo','doing','waiting','done') default 'todo'
>    - add priority with check in ('P0','P1','P2','P3') default 'P2'
> 4) updates documents:
>    - add phase_id NOT NULL referencing phases
>    - replace file_path with storage_bucket + storage_path (keep file_path but mark deprecated if needed)
> 5) updates templates and drafts:
>    - add phase_id NOT NULL referencing phases
> 6) updates packets:
>    - add phase_id NOT NULL referencing phases
>    - add packet_type check in ('efile','judge_copy','service','dispute','regulator','internal')
>    - constrain status check in ('building','ready','submitted','sent')
> 7) updates packet_items:
>    - add check constraint enforcing exactly one of document_id or draft_id is set
> 8) replaces envelopes fields to support efile:
>    - add phase_id
>    - court_system
>    - status ('draft','submitted','accepted','rejected')
>    - confirmation_number, rejection_reason, notes
>    - drop recipient_email/recipient_name ONLY if safe; otherwise leave but unused
> 9) add indexes:
>    tasks(user_id, phase_id, status)
>    documents(user_id, phase_id)
>    packet_items(packet_id, sort_order)
>    envelope_packets(envelope_id)
> 
> Return only the SQL in one code block. No commentary.
> ```
>

>

### User
> i already ran everything from the migration files so i need one to make these correcitons your mentioned here.

### Assistant
> Got it. Since you already ran the original migrations, you need a **new patch migration** that:
> 
> - **adds missing columns** (phase scoping, storage fields, envelope e-file fields)
> - **backfills** existing rows so constraints won’t fail
> - **normalizes** existing status values to the new controlled sets
> - **adds CHECK constraints + indexes**
> - does **not** drop anything risky (especially not envelope recipient fields)
> 
> Below is a single “do it once” patch migration you can run safely.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## `supabase/migrations/0005_patch_case_ops_schema.sql`
> 
> ```sql
> BEGIN;
> 
> -- 0) Enable pgcrypto for gen_random_uuid() (recommended; does not break existing uuid-ossp usage)
> CREATE EXTENSION IF NOT EXISTS pgcrypto;
> 
> -- 1) phases: restrict id to known set ('01'..'06')
> -- If you already inserted other phase ids, this will fail.
> -- We add constraint only after ensuring phase ids are valid.
> DO $$
> BEGIN
>   -- If phases table contains invalid ids, this will raise and stop the migration.
>   IF EXISTS (
>     SELECT 1 FROM phases
>     WHERE id NOT IN ('01','02','03','04','05','06')
>   ) THEN
>     RAISE EXCEPTION 'phases contains invalid id(s). Fix phases.id values before applying constraint.';
>   END IF;
> END $$;
> 
> ALTER TABLE phases
>   ADD CONSTRAINT phases_id_allowed_chk
>   CHECK (id IN ('01','02','03','04','05','06'));
> 
> -- 2) tasks: normalize status + add priority + constrain status
> -- Add priority column if missing
> ALTER TABLE tasks
>   ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS priority text;
> 
> -- Backfill priority
> UPDATE tasks
> SET priority = COALESCE(priority, 'P2')
> WHERE priority IS NULL;
> 
> -- Normalize task status values to controlled set
> -- Current defaults include 'pending'. Map common variants.
> UPDATE tasks
> SET status = 'todo'
> WHERE status IS NULL OR status IN ('pending','new','open');
> 
> UPDATE tasks
> SET status = 'doing'
> WHERE status IN ('in_progress','in progress','active','working');
> 
> UPDATE tasks
> SET status = 'waiting'
> WHERE status IN ('blocked','hold','paused','waiting');
> 
> UPDATE tasks
> SET status = 'done'
> WHERE status IN ('completed','complete','closed','resolved','finished');
> 
> -- If anything else exists, force to 'todo' to avoid constraint failure
> UPDATE tasks
> SET status = 'todo'
> WHERE status NOT IN ('todo','doing','waiting','done');
> 
> -- Ensure phase_id exists and is NOT NULL
> -- If any tasks have null phase_id, default them to '01' so we can enforce NOT NULL.
> UPDATE tasks
> SET phase_id = '01'
> WHERE phase_id IS NULL;
> 
> ALTER TABLE tasks
>   ALTER COLUMN phase_id SET NOT NULL;
> 
> -- Add constraints (only if not already present)
> DO $$
> BEGIN
>   IF NOT EXISTS (
>     SELECT 1 FROM pg_constraint WHERE conname = 'tasks_status_allowed_chk'
>   ) THEN
>     ALTER TABLE tasks
>       ADD CONSTRAINT tasks_status_allowed_chk
>       CHECK (status IN ('todo','doing','waiting','done'));
>   END IF;
> 
>   IF NOT EXISTS (
>     SELECT 1 FROM pg_constraint WHERE conname = 'tasks_priority_allowed_chk'
>   ) THEN
>     ALTER TABLE tasks
>       ADD CONSTRAINT tasks_priority_allowed_chk
>       CHECK (priority IN ('P0','P1','P2','P3'));
>   END IF;
> END $$;
> 
> -- 3) documents: add phase_id + storage_bucket/storage_path fields
> ALTER TABLE documents
>   ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS phase_id text,
>   ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS storage_bucket text,
>   ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS storage_path text;
> 
> -- Backfill documents.phase_id from task_id where possible
> UPDATE documents d
> SET phase_id = t.phase_id
> FROM tasks t
> WHERE d.phase_id IS NULL
>   AND d.task_id IS NOT NULL
>   AND d.task_id = t.id;
> 
> -- Default remaining null phase_id to '01' (you can recategorize later)
> UPDATE documents
> SET phase_id = '01'
> WHERE phase_id IS NULL;
> 
> -- Backfill storage_* from existing file_path if present
> -- Heuristic: store everything in 'documents' bucket and use file_path as path.
> UPDATE documents
> SET storage_bucket = COALESCE(storage_bucket, 'documents'),
>     storage_path   = COALESCE(storage_path, file_path)
> WHERE storage_bucket IS NULL OR storage_path IS NULL;
> 
> -- Enforce NOT NULL + FK after backfill
> ALTER TABLE documents
>   ALTER COLUMN phase_id SET NOT NULL;
> 
> DO $$
> BEGIN
>   IF NOT EXISTS (
>     SELECT 1 FROM pg_constraint WHERE conname = 'documents_phase_fk'
>   ) THEN
>     ALTER TABLE documents
>       ADD CONSTRAINT documents_phase_fk
>       FOREIGN KEY (phase_id) REFERENCES phases(id) ON DELETE RESTRICT;
>   END IF;
> END $$;
> 
> -- 4) templates: add phase_id, constrain to phases
> ALTER TABLE templates
>   ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS phase_id text;
> 
> UPDATE templates
> SET phase_id = '01'
> WHERE phase_id IS NULL;
> 
> ALTER TABLE templates
>   ALTER COLUMN phase_id SET NOT NULL;
> 
> DO $$
> BEGIN
>   IF NOT EXISTS (
>     SELECT 1 FROM pg_constraint WHERE conname = 'templates_phase_fk'
>   ) THEN
>     ALTER TABLE templates
>       ADD CONSTRAINT templates_phase_fk
>       FOREIGN KEY (phase_id) REFERENCES phases(id) ON DELETE RESTRICT;
>   END IF;
> END $$;
> 
> -- 5) drafts: add phase_id + constrain status
> ALTER TABLE drafts
>   ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS phase_id text;
> 
> -- Backfill drafts.phase_id from template_id where possible
> UPDATE drafts d
> SET phase_id = t.phase_id
> FROM templates t
> WHERE d.phase_id IS NULL
>   AND d.template_id IS NOT NULL
>   AND d.template_id = t.id;
> 
> -- Default remaining
> UPDATE drafts
> SET phase_id = '01'
> WHERE phase_id IS NULL;
> 
> ALTER TABLE drafts
>   ALTER COLUMN phase_id SET NOT NULL;
> 
> DO $$
> BEGIN
>   IF NOT EXISTS (
>     SELECT 1 FROM pg_constraint WHERE conname = 'drafts_phase_fk'
>   ) THEN
>     ALTER TABLE drafts
>       ADD CONSTRAINT drafts_phase_fk
>       FOREIGN KEY (phase_id) REFERENCES phases(id) ON DELETE RESTRICT;
>   END IF;
> END $$;
> 
> -- Normalize drafts.status
> UPDATE drafts
> SET status = 'draft'
> WHERE status IS NULL OR status IN ('pending','new','open');
> 
> UPDATE drafts
> SET status = 'ready'
> WHERE status IN ('final','ready_to_file','ready to file','ready-to-file');
> 
> UPDATE drafts
> SET status = 'filed'
> WHERE status IN ('submitted','filed_with_court','filed with court');
> 
> UPDATE drafts
> SET status = 'draft'
> WHERE status NOT IN ('draft','ready','filed');
> 
> DO $$
> BEGIN
>   IF NOT EXISTS (
>     SELECT 1 FROM pg_constraint WHERE conname = 'drafts_status_allowed_chk'
>   ) THEN
>     ALTER TABLE drafts
>       ADD CONSTRAINT drafts_status_allowed_chk
>       CHECK (status IN ('draft','ready','filed'));
>   END IF;
> END $$;
> 
> -- 6) packets: add phase_id + packet_type + constrain status
> ALTER TABLE packets
>   ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS phase_id text,
>   ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS packet_type text;
> 
> UPDATE packets
> SET phase_id = '01'
> WHERE phase_id IS NULL;
> 
> -- Default packet_type; you can refine later
> UPDATE packets
> SET packet_type = COALESCE(packet_type, 'internal')
> WHERE packet_type IS NULL;
> 
> -- Normalize packets.status
> UPDATE packets
> SET status = 'building'
> WHERE status IS NULL OR status IN ('open','pending','new');
> 
> UPDATE packets
> SET status = 'ready'
> WHERE status IN ('final','prepared');
> 
> UPDATE packets
> SET status = 'submitted'
> WHERE status IN ('filed','efile','e-file','submitted_to_court');
> 
> UPDATE packets
> SET status = 'sent'
> WHERE status IN ('served','emailed','mailed');
> 
> UPDATE packets
> SET status = 'building'
> WHERE status NOT IN ('building','ready','submitted','sent');
> 
> ALTER TABLE packets
>   ALTER COLUMN phase_id SET NOT NULL,
>   ALTER COLUMN packet_type SET NOT NULL;
> 
> DO $$
> BEGIN
>   IF NOT EXISTS (
>     SELECT 1 FROM pg_constraint WHERE conname = 'packets_phase_fk'
>   ) THEN
>     ALTER TABLE packets
>       ADD CONSTRAINT packets_phase_fk
>       FOREIGN KEY (phase_id) REFERENCES phases(id) ON DELETE RESTRICT;
>   END IF;
> 
>   IF NOT EXISTS (
>     SELECT 1 FROM pg_constraint WHERE conname = 'packets_status_allowed_chk'
>   ) THEN
>     ALTER TABLE packets
>       ADD CONSTRAINT packets_status_allowed_chk
>       CHECK (status IN ('building','ready','submitted','sent'));
>   END IF;
> 
>   IF NOT EXISTS (
>     SELECT 1 FROM pg_constraint WHERE conname = 'packets_type_allowed_chk'
>   ) THEN
>     ALTER TABLE packets
>       ADD CONSTRAINT packets_type_allowed_chk
>       CHECK (packet_type IN ('efile','judge_copy','service','dispute','regulator','internal'));
>   END IF;
> END $$;
> 
> -- 7) packet_items: enforce XOR rule (exactly one of document_id or draft_id)
> -- Some legacy rows might have both null or both set; fix them first.
> 
> -- If both are null, delete (nothing to reference)
> DELETE FROM packet_items
> WHERE document_id IS NULL AND draft_id IS NULL;
> 
> -- If both set, keep document_id and null draft_id (arbitrary but stable)
> UPDATE packet_items
> SET draft_id = NULL
> WHERE document_id IS NOT NULL AND draft_id IS NOT NULL;
> 
> DO $$
> BEGIN
>   IF NOT EXISTS (
>     SELECT 1 FROM pg_constraint WHERE conname = 'packet_items_xor_chk'
>   ) THEN
>     ALTER TABLE packet_items
>       ADD CONSTRAINT packet_items_xor_chk
>       CHECK (
>         (document_id IS NOT NULL AND draft_id IS NULL)
>         OR
>         (document_id IS NULL AND draft_id IS NOT NULL)
>       );
>   END IF;
> END $$;
> 
> -- 8) envelopes: convert to e-file tracking by ADDING fields (do not drop recipient fields)
> ALTER TABLE envelopes
>   ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS phase_id text,
>   ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS court_system text,
>   ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS confirmation_number text,
>   ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS rejection_reason text,
>   ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS notes text;
> 
> -- Normalize envelope.status to efile statuses
> UPDATE envelopes
> SET status = 'draft'
> WHERE status IS NULL OR status IN ('prepared','open','pending');
> 
> UPDATE envelopes
> SET status = 'submitted'
> WHERE status IN ('sent','filed','efile','e-file','submitted');
> 
> UPDATE envelopes
> SET status = 'accepted'
> WHERE status IN ('approved','ok','successful');
> 
> UPDATE envelopes
> SET status = 'rejected'
> WHERE status IN ('failed','denied','error');
> 
> UPDATE envelopes
> SET status = 'draft'
> WHERE status NOT IN ('draft','submitted','accepted','rejected');
> 
> -- Backfill envelopes.phase_id with default '01' (can be updated later)
> UPDATE envelopes
> SET phase_id = '01'
> WHERE phase_id IS NULL;
> 
> ALTER TABLE envelopes
>   ALTER COLUMN phase_id SET NOT NULL;
> 
> DO $$
> BEGIN
>   IF NOT EXISTS (
>     SELECT 1 FROM pg_constraint WHERE conname = 'envelopes_phase_fk'
>   ) THEN
>     ALTER TABLE envelopes
>       ADD CONSTRAINT envelopes_phase_fk
>       FOREIGN KEY (phase_id) REFERENCES phases(id) ON DELETE RESTRICT;
>   END IF;
> 
>   IF NOT EXISTS (
>     SELECT 1 FROM pg_constraint WHERE conname = 'envelopes_status_allowed_chk'
>   ) THEN
>     ALTER TABLE envelopes
>       ADD CONSTRAINT envelopes_status_allowed_chk
>       CHECK (status IN ('draft','submitted','accepted','rejected'));
>   END IF;
> END $$;
> 
> -- 9) packet_exports: add storage_bucket/storage_path to avoid brittle URLs
> ALTER TABLE packet_exports
>   ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS storage_bucket text,
>   ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS storage_path text,
>   ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS export_type text;
> 
> -- Backfill export fields
> UPDATE packet_exports
> SET storage_bucket = COALESCE(storage_bucket, 'exports'),
>     storage_path   = COALESCE(storage_path, export_url),
>     export_type    = COALESCE(export_type, 'internal')
> WHERE storage_bucket IS NULL OR storage_path IS NULL OR export_type IS NULL;
> 
> DO $$
> BEGIN
>   IF NOT EXISTS (
>     SELECT 1 FROM pg_constraint WHERE conname = 'packet_exports_type_allowed_chk'
>   ) THEN
>     ALTER TABLE packet_exports
>       ADD CONSTRAINT packet_exports_type_allowed_chk
>       CHECK (export_type IN ('judge_copy','opposing_counsel','service','internal'));
>   END IF;
> 
>   IF NOT EXISTS (
>     SELECT 1 FROM pg_constraint WHERE conname = 'packet_exports_format_allowed_chk'
>   ) THEN
>     ALTER TABLE packet_exports
>       ADD CONSTRAINT packet_exports_format_allowed_chk
>       CHECK (format IN ('pdf','zip'));
>   END IF;
> END $$;
> 
> -- 10) Indexes (safe, idempotent)
> CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_tasks_user_phase_status
>   ON tasks (user_id, phase_id, status);
> 
> CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_documents_user_phase
>   ON documents (user_id, phase_id);
> 
> CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_packet_items_packet_sort
>   ON packet_items (packet_id, sort_order);
> 
> CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_envelope_packets_envelope
>   ON envelope_packets (envelope_id);
> 
> COMMIT;
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Two important realities (so you don’t get surprised)
> 
> ### A) This migration defaults missing `phase_id` to `'01'`
> That’s intentional so the constraints can be enforced without blocking. You can reassign phases later via the app UI.
> 
> ### B) I did not drop any columns
> - `documents.file_path` stays (even though we prefer `storage_bucket/storage_path`)
> - `envelopes.recipient_email/recipient_name` stay
> - `packet_exports.export_url` stays
> 
> Dropping can destroy data; we don’t do that in a hot system.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Next step
> 1) Save this as `0005_patch_case_ops_schema.sql`
> 2) Run it in Supabase SQL Editor
> 3) Then paste your **0003_rls.sql** and **0004_storage.sql** contents (even if already applied), because we need to confirm your policies still align with the new columns (`phase_id`, `storage_bucket`, etc.)
> 
> If you want, I can also give you a follow-up migration that:
> - migrates old `file_path` into `storage_path` more cleanly,
> - and optionally deprecates/remove email-envelope fields once you’re sure you don’t need them.

> all tables are build. -- WARNING: This schema is for context only and is not meant to be run.
