> CREATE TABLE public.documents (

>   id uuid NOT NULL DEFAULT uuid_generate_v4(),

>   user_id uuid NOT NULL DEFAULT auth.uid(),

>   task_id uuid,

>   title text NOT NULL,

>   file_path text,

>   file_type text,

>   size_bytes bigint,

>   metadata jsonb DEFAULT '{}'::jsonb,

>   created_at timestamp with time zone DEFAULT now(),

>   updated_at timestamp with time zone DEFAULT now(),

>   phase_id text NOT NULL,

>   storage_bucket text,

>   storage_path text,

>   CONSTRAINT documents_pkey PRIMARY KEY (id),

>   CONSTRAINT documents_task_id_fkey FOREIGN KEY (task_id) REFERENCES public.tasks(id),

>   CONSTRAINT documents_phase_fk FOREIGN KEY (phase_id) REFERENCES public.phases(id)

> );

> CREATE TABLE public.drafts (

>   id uuid NOT NULL DEFAULT uuid_generate_v4(),

>   user_id uuid NOT NULL DEFAULT auth.uid(),

>   template_id uuid,

>   title text,

>   content_data jsonb DEFAULT '{}'::jsonb,

>   status text DEFAULT 'draft'::text CHECK (status = ANY (ARRAY['draft'::text, 'ready'::text, 'filed'::text])),

>   created_at timestamp with time zone DEFAULT now(),

>   updated_at timestamp with time zone DEFAULT now(),

>   phase_id text NOT NULL,

>   CONSTRAINT drafts_pkey PRIMARY KEY (id),

>   CONSTRAINT drafts_template_id_fkey FOREIGN KEY (template_id) REFERENCES public.templates(id),

>   CONSTRAINT drafts_phase_fk FOREIGN KEY (phase_id) REFERENCES public.phases(id)

> );

> CREATE TABLE public.envelope_packets (

>   id uuid NOT NULL DEFAULT uuid_generate_v4(),

>   user_id uuid NOT NULL DEFAULT auth.uid(),

>   envelope_id uuid,

>   packet_id uuid,

>   created_at timestamp with time zone DEFAULT now(),

>   updated_at timestamp with time zone DEFAULT now(),

>   CONSTRAINT envelope_packets_pkey PRIMARY KEY (id),

>   CONSTRAINT envelope_packets_envelope_id_fkey FOREIGN KEY (envelope_id) REFERENCES public.envelopes(id),

>   CONSTRAINT envelope_packets_packet_id_fkey FOREIGN KEY (packet_id) REFERENCES public.packets(id)

> );

> CREATE TABLE public.envelopes (

>   id uuid NOT NULL DEFAULT uuid_generate_v4(),

>   user_id uuid NOT NULL DEFAULT auth.uid(),

>   recipient_email text,

>   recipient_name text,

>   status text DEFAULT 'prepared'::text CHECK (status = ANY (ARRAY['draft'::text, 'submitted'::text, 'accepted'::text, 'rejected'::text])),

>   sent_at timestamp with time zone,

>   created_at timestamp with time zone DEFAULT now(),

>   updated_at timestamp with time zone DEFAULT now(),

>   phase_id text NOT NULL,

>   court_system text,

>   confirmation_number text,

>   rejection_reason text,

>   notes text,

>   CONSTRAINT envelopes_pkey PRIMARY KEY (id),

>   CONSTRAINT envelopes_phase_fk FOREIGN KEY (phase_id) REFERENCES public.phases(id)

> );

> CREATE TABLE public.packet_exports (

>   id uuid NOT NULL DEFAULT uuid_generate_v4(),

>   user_id uuid NOT NULL DEFAULT auth.uid(),

>   packet_id uuid,

>   export_url text,

>   format text DEFAULT 'pdf'::text CHECK (format = ANY (ARRAY['pdf'::text, 'zip'::text])),

>   status text DEFAULT 'processing'::text,

>   completed_at timestamp with time zone,

>   created_at timestamp with time zone DEFAULT now(),

>   updated_at timestamp with time zone DEFAULT now(),

>   storage_bucket text,

>   storage_path text,

>   export_type text CHECK (export_type = ANY (ARRAY['judge_copy'::text, 'opposing_counsel'::text, 'service'::text, 'internal'::text])),

>   CONSTRAINT packet_exports_pkey PRIMARY KEY (id),

>   CONSTRAINT packet_exports_packet_id_fkey FOREIGN KEY (packet_id) REFERENCES public.packets(id)

> );

> CREATE TABLE public.packet_items (

>   id uuid NOT NULL DEFAULT uuid_generate_v4(),

>   user_id uuid NOT NULL DEFAULT auth.uid(),

>   packet_id uuid,

>   document_id uuid,

>   draft_id uuid,

>   sort_order integer DEFAULT 0,

>   created_at timestamp with time zone DEFAULT now(),

>   updated_at timestamp with time zone DEFAULT now(),

>   CONSTRAINT packet_items_pkey PRIMARY KEY (id),

>   CONSTRAINT packet_items_packet_id_fkey FOREIGN KEY (packet_id) REFERENCES public.packets(id),

>   CONSTRAINT packet_items_document_id_fkey FOREIGN KEY (document_id) REFERENCES public.documents(id),

>   CONSTRAINT packet_items_draft_id_fkey FOREIGN KEY (draft_id) REFERENCES public.drafts(id)

> );

> CREATE TABLE public.packets (

>   id uuid NOT NULL DEFAULT uuid_generate_v4(),

>   user_id uuid NOT NULL DEFAULT auth.uid(),

>   name text NOT NULL,

>   description text,

>   status text DEFAULT 'open'::text CHECK (status = ANY (ARRAY['building'::text, 'ready'::text, 'submitted'::text, 'sent'::text])),

>   version integer DEFAULT 1,

>   created_at timestamp with time zone DEFAULT now(),

>   updated_at timestamp with time zone DEFAULT now(),

>   phase_id text NOT NULL,

>   packet_type text NOT NULL CHECK (packet_type = ANY (ARRAY['efile'::text, 'judge_copy'::text, 'service'::text, 'dispute'::text, 'regulator'::text, 'internal'::text])),

>   CONSTRAINT packets_pkey PRIMARY KEY (id),

>   CONSTRAINT packets_phase_fk FOREIGN KEY (phase_id) REFERENCES public.phases(id)

> );

> CREATE TABLE public.phases (

>   id text NOT NULL CHECK (id = ANY (ARRAY['01'::text, '02'::text, '03'::text, '04'::text, '05'::text, '06'::text])),

>   name text NOT NULL,

>   description text,

>   created_at timestamp with time zone DEFAULT now(),

>   updated_at timestamp with time zone DEFAULT now(),

>   CONSTRAINT phases_pkey PRIMARY KEY (id)

> );

> CREATE TABLE public.tasks (

>   id uuid NOT NULL DEFAULT uuid_generate_v4(),

>   user_id uuid NOT NULL DEFAULT auth.uid(),

>   phase_id text NOT NULL,

>   title text NOT NULL,

>   description text,

>   status text DEFAULT 'pending'::text CHECK (status = ANY (ARRAY['todo'::text, 'doing'::text, 'waiting'::text, 'done'::text])),

>   due_date timestamp with time zone,

>   created_at timestamp with time zone DEFAULT now(),

>   updated_at timestamp with time zone DEFAULT now(),

>   priority text CHECK (priority = ANY (ARRAY['P0'::text, 'P1'::text, 'P2'::text, 'P3'::text])),

>   CONSTRAINT tasks_pkey PRIMARY KEY (id),

>   CONSTRAINT tasks_phase_id_fkey FOREIGN KEY (phase_id) REFERENCES public.phases(id)

> );

> CREATE TABLE public.templates (

>   id uuid NOT NULL DEFAULT uuid_generate_v4(),

>   user_id uuid NOT NULL DEFAULT auth.uid(),

>   name text NOT NULL,

>   content text,

>   category text,

>   is_active boolean DEFAULT true,

>   created_at timestamp with time zone DEFAULT now(),

>   updated_at timestamp with time zone DEFAULT now(),

>   phase_id text NOT NULL,

>   CONSTRAINT templates_pkey PRIMARY KEY (id),

>   CONSTRAINT templates_phase_fk FOREIGN KEY (phase_id) REFERENCES public.phases(id)

> );

### Assistant
> Perfect — thank you for pasting the **actual post-migration schema**. This lets me give you a clean, authoritative answer.
> 
> Short version first, then details:
> 
> > **You are 85–90% solid. The core model is correct.  
> > There are 5 specific fixes / tighten-ups you should do now, and then you should STOP touching schema and move to UI + RLS verification.**
> 
> I’ll be very explicit and surgical.
> 
> ---
> 
> # ✅ What is GOOD (and locked)
> 
> You did these right — do **not** change them now:
> 
> - Phase-scoped everything (`phase_id` on tasks, documents, drafts, templates, packets, envelopes)
> - Packet → packet_items → documents/drafts model
> - Envelope ↔ packet join table (supports multi-packet filings)
> - Controlled CHECK constraints on:
>   - `tasks.status`
>   - `drafts.status`
>   - `packets.status`
>   - `packet_type`
> - Keeping legacy columns (`file_path`, `recipient_email`) instead of deleting
> - UUIDs + `auth.uid()` everywhere
> 
> This is **not** a toy schema. It’s production-grade.
> 
> ---
> 
> # 🚨 What still needs fixing (real issues)
> 
> ## 1️⃣ `tasks.status` default is WRONG (will violate its own CHECK)
> 
> ```sql
> status text DEFAULT 'pending' CHECK (status IN ('todo','doing','waiting','done'))
> ```
> 
> This is a **hard bug**.
> 
> ### Fix (must do)
> ```sql
> ALTER TABLE tasks
>   ALTER COLUMN status SET DEFAULT 'todo';
> ```
> 
> If you do nothing else, do this.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 2️⃣ `packet_items` is missing the XOR constraint (integrity hole)
> 
> Right now, nothing prevents:
> - both `document_id` and `draft_id` being NULL
> - both being set
> 
> That **will** cause silent corruption later.
> 
> ### Fix (safe, additive)
> ```sql
> ALTER TABLE packet_items
> ADD CONSTRAINT packet_items_xor_chk
> CHECK (
>   (document_id IS NOT NULL AND draft_id IS NULL)
>   OR
>   (document_id IS NULL AND draft_id IS NOT NULL)
> );
> ```
> 
> If this fails, it means you already have bad rows — tell me and we’ll clean them first.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 3️⃣ `documents.storage_*` should be NOT NULL (you already depend on them)
> 
> You already backfilled them. Lock it in.
> 
> ### Fix
> ```sql
> ALTER TABLE documents
>   ALTER COLUMN storage_bucket SET NOT NULL,
>   ALTER COLUMN storage_path SET NOT NULL;
> ```
> 
> This prevents “uploaded but not renderable” bugs on mobile.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 4️⃣ `packet_exports.status` is unconstrained (dangerous later)
> 
> Right now:
> ```sql
> status text DEFAULT 'processing'
> ```
> 
> You will eventually branch UI logic on this — constrain it now.
> 
> ### Fix
> ```sql
> ALTER TABLE packet_exports
> ADD CONSTRAINT packet_exports_status_chk
> CHECK (status IN ('processing','ready','failed'));
> ```
> 
> Optional but recommended.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 5️⃣ Missing **indexes** for performance (cheap win)
> 
> Add these — they won’t break anything and will matter once you have data.
> 
> ```sql
> CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_tasks_user_phase_status
>   ON tasks (user_id, phase_id, status);
> 
> CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_documents_user_phase
>   ON documents (user_id, phase_id);
> 
> CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_packet_items_packet_sort
>   ON packet_items (packet_id, sort_order);
> 
> CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_envelope_packets_envelope
>   ON envelope_packets (envelope_id);
> ```
>

### User
> number 2 failed

### Assistant
> Yep — that means you already have **at least one** `packet_items` row that violates the XOR rule.
> 
> We’re going to (1) identify the bad rows, (2) fix them in a way that doesn’t destroy useful data, then (3) re-add the constraint.
> 
> No drama.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 1) Find exactly what’s violating XOR
> 
> Run this:
> 
> ```sql
> -- Rows where BOTH are NULL (invalid)
> select id, packet_id, document_id, draft_id, sort_order, created_at
> from packet_items
> where document_id is null and draft_id is null
> order by created_at desc;
> 
> -- Rows where BOTH are set (invalid)
> select id, packet_id, document_id, draft_id, sort_order, created_at
> from packet_items
> where document_id is not null and draft_id is not null
> order by created_at desc;
> ```
> 
> If either query returns rows, that’s your failure.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 2) Fix strategy (safe defaults)
> 
> ### A) If both are NULL  
> Those rows don’t point to anything. They are junk placeholders.
> 
> **Delete them:**
> ```sql
> delete from packet_items
> where document_id is null and draft_id is null;
> ```
> 
> ### B) If both are set  
> Pick a deterministic rule. For MVP, I recommend **prefer document**, null out draft.
> 
> **Fix them:**
> ```sql
> update packet_items
> set draft_id = null
> where document_id is not null and draft_id is not null;
> ```
> 
> If you’d rather prefer draft, flip it (set document_id = null). But choose one rule and stick to it.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 3) Re-apply the XOR constraint
> 
> Now rerun:
> 
> ```sql
> alter table packet_items
> add constraint packet_items_xor_chk
> check (
>   (document_id is not null and draft_id is null)
>   or
>   (document_id is null and draft_id is not null)
> );
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 4) If it STILL fails (rare, but possible)
> Then there are rows where `document_id` or `draft_id` points to a record that got deleted, causing confusion. Check for orphans:
> 
> ```sql
> -- packet_items with document_id that doesn't exist
> select pi.*
> from packet_items pi
> left join documents d on d.id = pi.document_id
> where pi.document_id is not null and d.id is null;
> 
> -- packet_items with draft_id that doesn't exist
> select pi.*
> from packet_items pi
> left join drafts dr on dr.id = pi.draft_id
> where pi.draft_id is not null and dr.id is null;
> ```
> 
> If you see results, delete those broken rows:
> 
> ```sql
> delete from packet_items pi
> using documents d
> where pi.document_id is not null
>   and d.id is null;  -- (this exact form doesn't work; use the select above then delete by id)
> ```
> 
> Safer: delete by IDs from the select results.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Fast “do it all” block (if you want one-shot)
> If you don’t care about inspecting first and just want it fixed:
> 
> ```sql
> begin;
> 
> delete from packet_items
> where document_id is null and draft_id is null;
> 
> update packet_items
> set draft_id = null
> where document_id is not null and draft_id is not null;
> 
> alter table packet_items
> add constraint packet_items_xor_chk
> check (
>   (document_id is not null and draft_id is null)
>   or
>   (document_id is null and draft_id is not null)
> );
> 
> commit;
> ```
>

### User
> i got the magic link but it just took me right back to the login screen asking for my email

### Assistant
> Good catch. This is a **classic Supabase magic-link miswire**, not a schema issue. We’ll fix it cleanly.
> 
> What you’re seeing means **auth succeeded**, but the app **never persisted or read the session**, so it dumped you back to `/login`.
> 
> There are **four common causes**. We’ll go in the exact order that resolves this fastest.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Step 1 — Confirm Supabase auth settings (30 seconds)
> 
> In **Supabase Dashboard → Authentication → URL Configuration**:
> 
> Check **all three** of these:
> 
> 1. **Site URL**  
>    Must exactly match where the app is running, e.g.
>    ```
>    https://your-app.pages.dev
>    ```
>    or
>    ```
>    http://localhost:5173
>    ```
> 
> 2. **Redirect URLs**  
>    Add BOTH:
>    ```
>    http://localhost:5173/**
>    https://your-app.pages.dev/**
>    ```
> 
> 3. **Email link type**
>    - Magic link: ✅ enabled
>    - OTP only: ❌ (unless intentional)
> 
> If this is wrong, Supabase will authenticate you… then drop the session.
> 
> Fix this first if needed.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Step 2 — Your app is not restoring the session
> 
> This is the **most likely culprit**.
> 
> If your app does **not** do BOTH of the following, you’ll loop forever:
> 
> - Read existing session on load
> - Listen for auth state changes
> 
> ### Required code (this is non-optional)
> 
> In `src/lib/supabase.ts`:
> 
> ```ts
> import { createClient } from '@supabase/supabase-js'
> 
> export const supabase = createClient(
>   import.meta.env.VITE_SUPABASE_URL!,
>   import.meta.env.VITE_SUPABASE_ANON_KEY!,
>   {
>     auth: {
>       persistSession: true,
>       autoRefreshToken: true,
>       detectSessionInUrl: true
>     }
>   }
> )
> ```
> 
> If `detectSessionInUrl` is missing → **magic link is ignored**.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Step 3 — Your app is probably redirecting too early
> 
> This bug happens when you do something like:
> 
> ```ts
> if (!session) navigate('/login')
> ```
> 
> **before Supabase finishes restoring the session.**
> 
> ### Correct pattern (this matters)
> 
> In your top-level app (usually `App.tsx` or `AuthProvider.tsx`):
> 
> ```ts
> const [loading, setLoading] = useState(true)
> const [session, setSession] = useState<Session | null>(null)
> 
> useEffect(() => {
>   supabase.auth.getSession().then(({ data }) => {
>     setSession(data.session)
>     setLoading(false)
>   })
> 
>   const { data: listener } = supabase.auth.onAuthStateChange(
>     (_event, session) => {
>       setSession(session)
>     }
>   )
> 
>   return () => listener.subscription.unsubscribe()
> }, [])
> 
> if (loading) return null  // or spinner
> ```
> 
> Then—and **only then**—do routing logic:
> 
> ```ts
> if (!session) return <Login />
> return <Dashboard />
> ```
> 
> If you skip the loading guard, you get exactly the behavior you’re seeing.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Step 4 — Verify this is not an RLS illusion (quick test)
> 
> If auth works but RLS blocks everything, your UI might *think* you’re logged out.
> 
> Run this in Supabase **SQL Editor → Run as authenticated user**:
> 
> ```sql
> select auth.uid();
> ```
> 
> - If this returns a UUID → auth is fine
> - If NULL → session is not attached
> 
> Also try:
> 
> ```sql
> select count(*) from tasks;
> ```
> 
> If it errors with “permission denied” → RLS is wrong  
> If it returns `0` → auth is fine, data just empty
> 
> ---
> 
> ## The fastest way to confirm where it’s broken
> 
> Answer **just one** of these:
> 
> 1. Do you see `#access_token=` in the URL when clicking the magic link?
> 2. Do you have `detectSessionInUrl: true` set?
> 3. Are you redirecting to `/login` before `getSession()` resolves?
> 
> Based on that, I’ll tell you **exactly which line to fix**.
> 
> You’re very close — this is not a big failure, it’s a standard auth wiring hiccup.

### User
> im getting a blank screen still even after doing that you said.

### Assistant
> Blank screen after adding the “loading/session” guard usually means one of three things:
> 
> 1) **Your app is throwing a runtime error** (most common)  
> 2) **You’re returning `null` forever** because `setLoading(false)` never runs  
> 3) **Your routing/layout is rendering nothing** due to a logic branch
> 
> We’ll debug this in a tight, deterministic way.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Step 1 — Open the browser console (this is non-negotiable)
> On desktop: **F12 → Console**  
> On phone (if needed): open it on desktop first; mobile console is a pain.
> 
> Tell me the **first red error** you see. If you paste it verbatim, I’ll pinpoint the fix.
> 
> While you’re there, also check **Network** for failed JS file loads (404s).
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Step 2 — Add a “panic banner” so you can see where it’s dying
> Put this at the very top of `App.tsx` render (first line inside the component return), temporarily:
> 
> ```tsx
> return (
>   <div style={{ padding: 16, fontFamily: 'system-ui' }}>
>     <h1>CASE OPS DEBUG</h1>
>     <pre>{JSON.stringify({ loading, hasSession: !!session }, null, 2)}</pre>
>   </div>
> )
> ```
> 
> If you still see blank, the app is failing **before** rendering (build/runtime error).
> 
> If you see it and it says `loading: true` forever, then `getSession()` isn’t completing or you threw inside the effect.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Step 3 — Hard-check your env vars (most common Cloudflare issue)
> A blank screen often happens because Supabase client init throws when env vars are undefined.
> 
> In `src/lib/supabase.ts`, temporarily log:
> 
> ```ts
> console.log("SUPABASE URL?", import.meta.env.VITE_SUPABASE_URL)
> console.log("SUPABASE KEY?", import.meta.env.VITE_SUPABASE_ANON_KEY ? "set" : "missing")
> ```
> 
> If URL is `undefined` or key is missing:
> - Cloudflare Pages env vars aren’t set for the correct environment (Preview vs Production), or
> - you didn’t redeploy after setting them.
> 
> Fix: Cloudflare Pages → Settings → Environment variables → set for **Production** and **Preview**, then redeploy.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Step 4 — Make sure you didn’t do `if (loading) return null` with no fallback
> That will look like a blank screen even when things are “working”.
> 
> Change it to:
> 
> ```tsx
> if (loading) return <div style={{ padding: 16 }}>Loading session…</div>
> ```
> 
> If it never leaves that state, your effect isn’t running or is crashing.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Step 5 — Confirm your `onAuthStateChange` unsubscribe isn’t wrong
> This trips people up depending on the SDK version. Use this exact pattern:
> 
> ```ts
> useEffect(() => {
>   let mounted = true;
> 
>   supabase.auth.getSession().then(({ data, error }) => {
>     if (!mounted) return;
>     if (error) console.error("getSession error", error);
>     setSession(data.session);
>     setLoading(false);
>   });
> 
>   const { data: { subscription } } = supabase.auth.onAuthStateChange((_event, session) => {
>     setSession(session);
>   });
> 
>   return () => {
>     mounted = false;
>     subscription.unsubscribe();
>   };
> }, []);
> ```
> 
> If you destructure wrong, it can throw and you’ll get blank.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Fastest path: you give me 2 things
> 1) The **first console error** (red)  
> 2) Whether `VITE_SUPABASE_URL` shows as **undefined** or not
> 
> That’s it. With those two, I can tell you exactly what’s broken.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## If you want the “brute force” test
> Comment out all routing and return only this:
> 
> ```tsx
> export default function App() {
>   return <div style={{ padding: 16 }}>App rendered</div>
> }
> ```
> 
> - If still blank → build/deploy issue (wrong output dir, broken JS load, Cloudflare config)
> - If shows → runtime auth/router logic issue
> 
> ---
> 
> Send the console error and env var result. This is fixable quickly, but not by guessing.

> ---
> 
> ## Why this is happening (plain English)
> 
> - Your code is correct enough to initialize Supabase
> - But when Cloudflare builds the app, it **does not have the env vars**

> ## The fix (do this in order, no skipping)
>

>

>

> 
> You must add **both variables** in **both environments**:
> 
> #### Production
> - `VITE_SUPABASE_URL` = `https://xxxx.supabase.co`
> - `VITE_SUPABASE_ANON_KEY` = `eyJhbGciOiJI...`
> 
> #### Preview
> - SAME two variables
> - SAME values
> 
> ⚠️ Cloudflare treats **Preview and Production separately**.  
> If you only set one, you still get this error.
> 
> ---
> 
> ### Step 2 — Redeploy (required)
> After setting env vars:
> 
> - Go to **Deployments**
> - Click **Retry deployment** (or push a dummy commit)
> 
> Cloudflare **does NOT inject env vars into existing builds**.
> 
> ---
> 
> ### Step 3 — Confirm Vite sees them (one-line test)
> 
> In `src/lib/supabase.ts`, temporarily add:
>

> console.log("SUPABASE KEY SET:", !!import.meta.env.VITE_SUPABASE_ANON_KEY)
> ```
> 
> Redeploy and open the site.
> 
> Expected:
> - URL prints correctly
> - KEY SET = `true`
> 
> If URL is still `undefined`, the env var is not wired correctly in Pages.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Common mistakes to avoid (these cause exactly this error)
> 
> - ❌ Using `SUPABASE_URL` instead of `VITE_SUPABASE_URL`
> - ❌ Forgetting to set **Preview** env vars
> - ❌ Not redeploying after adding env vars
> - ❌ Putting env vars only in local `.env` (Cloudflare ignores it)
>

>

>

> Cloudflare has:
> - **Production** URL (main)
> - **Preview** URLs (per deployment)
>

> const key = import.meta.env.VITE_SUPABASE_ANON_KEY
>

> ```

> Quick check:
> - In your repo, confirm `app/case-ops/package.json` exists.
> - If the Vite project is actually at `app/case-ops/` but you created it somewhere else, Cloudflare is building the wrong thing.
> 
> Symptom when it builds wrong dir: it deploys *something* but not the updated bundle.
> 
> ---

> console.log("ENV KEY SET", !!import.meta.env.VITE_SUPABASE_ANON_KEY)
> ```
> 
> Redeploy. Open the site. Console should show:
> - URL = `https://igaveicxkdqmjfxyakwb.supabase.co`
> - KEY SET = `true`

### User
> just found out they are hard coded they are not coming from supbase?

### Assistant
> Perfect catch. This is actually **good news**, because it means we can fix this cleanly **without touching the database again**.
> 
> Right now your situation is:
> 
> - ✅ Supabase schema is correct
> - ❌ UI phase labels are **hard-coded**
> - ⚠️ That will absolutely fight you later (and confuse ADHD-brain)
> 
> We’re going to **rip out the hard-coded phases** and make the UI **authoritative from Supabase**, *once*, in a controlled way.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## The rule going forward (non-negotiable)
> **Phases live in the database.  
> The UI only renders what Supabase returns.**
> 
> No enums. No arrays. No constants.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## What to search for right now (2 minutes)
> 
> In your repo, search for any of these patterns:
> 
> ```ts
> const phases = [
> ```
> 
> ```ts
> PHASES = [
> ```
> 
> ```ts
> [{ id: '01'
> ```
> 
> ```ts
> Phase 1:
> ```
> 
> ```ts
> Concept
> Draft
> Review
> Approval
> Execution
> Closure
> ```
> 
> You will almost certainly find something like:
> 
> ```ts
> const PHASES = [
>   { id: '01', name: 'Concept' },
>   { id: '02', name: 'Draft' },
>   ...
> ]
> ```
> 
> That entire structure needs to die.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## The correct architecture (minimal, ADHD-safe)
> 
> ### 1️⃣ Create ONE source of truth: `usePhases()`
> 
> Create this file:
> 
> ### `src/hooks/usePhases.ts`
> ```ts
> import { useEffect, useState } from 'react'
> import { supabase } from '../lib/supabase'
> 
> export interface Phase {
>   id: string
>   name: string
>   description?: string
> }
> 
> export function usePhases() {
>   const [phases, setPhases] = useState<Phase[]>([])
>   const [loading, setLoading] = useState(true)
> 
>   useEffect(() => {
>     let mounted = true
> 
>     supabase
>       .from('phases')
>       .select('id, name, description')
>       .order('id')
>       .then(({ data, error }) => {
>         if (error) {
>           console.error('Failed to load phases', error)
>           return
>         }
>         if (mounted && data) setPhases(data)
>       })
>       .finally(() => mounted && setLoading(false))
> 
>     return () => {
>       mounted = false
>     }
>   }, [])
> 
>   return { phases, loading }
> }
> ```
> 
> That’s it. No magic. No cleverness.
> 
> ---
> 
> ### 2️⃣ Replace the hard-coded phase nav
> 
> Wherever your phase nav lives (top bar / tabs), replace:
> 
> ❌ **This (bad):**
> ```ts
> PHASES.map(...)
> ```
> 
> ✅ **With this (good):**
> ```ts
> const { phases, loading } = usePhases()
> 
> if (loading) return null
> 
> return (
>   <nav>
>     {phases.map(p => (
>       <button key={p.id}>
>         {p.id} — {p.name}
>       </button>
>     ))}
>   </nav>
> )
> ```
> 
> Now:
> - Phase names update instantly when DB changes
> - No redeploy needed to rename a phase
> - Your UI can’t drift from reality
> 
> ---
> 
> ## IMPORTANT: map “subphases” correctly
> You were right earlier: what the UI showed were **subphases**, not case phases.
> 
> Here’s the correct mental model:
> 
> | Layer | Source | Example |
> |-----|------|-------|
> | **Phase** | `phases` table | `01 Foreclosure Core` |
> | **Subphase / Workflow** | UI only | Draft / Review / File |
> | **Task status** | `tasks.status` | todo / doing / waiting / done |
> 
> So:
> - **Do NOT** create subphases in DB
> - **Do NOT** encode workflow names as phases
> - Workflow = task status + packet status
> 
> That keeps the model simple and flexible.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Quick sanity test (do this)
> After wiring `usePhases()`:
> 
> 1. Change a phase name in Supabase:
>    ```sql
>    update phases set name = 'Foreclosure Core (LIVE TEST)' where id = '01';
>    ```
> 2. Refresh the app
> 3. If the UI updates → you’re done
> 
> Then revert the name.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Why this matters for ADHD
> Hard-coded phases:
> - create silent mismatch
> - cause “why does this feel wrong?” stress
> - require redeploys for conceptual changes
> 
> DB-driven phases:
> - let you rename/reframe as your strategy evolves
> - reduce cognitive friction
> - keep the system honest
> 
> ---
>

> 
> If you want, paste:
> - the file where phases are currently hard-coded  
> and I’ll tell you **exactly which lines to delete and replace**, no guessing.
> 
> You caught this at the right time. This was a real fork-in-the-road issue.

>     WHEN '03' THEN 'Property obligations: AES, Citizens, Shadow Pointe HOA, City of Indianapolis'

### Assistant

> 
> Here’s what’s next, in two parallel tracks:
> 
> 1) **Supabase: add minimal “phase state + gating”** (tiny schema patch)
> 2) **Gemini: update the app to enforce the ladder + generate phase-scoped tasks/templates**
>

> ---
> 
> # A) Supabase: minimal schema changes (do this next)
> 
> ## 1) Add `phase_state` table (this is the control panel)
> This avoids hacks like “special gating task.” It’s cleaner and keeps you in control.
> 
> Run:
> 
> ```sql
> begin;
> 
> create table if not exists phase_state (
>   id uuid primary key default uuid_generate_v4(),
>   user_id uuid not null default auth.uid(),
>   current_phase_id text not null references phases(id) on delete restrict,
>   settlement_phase_id text not null default '05' references phases(id) on delete restrict,
>   allow_settlement_jump boolean not null default true,
>   last_non_settlement_phase_id text,
>   updated_at timestamptz not null default now(),
>   created_at timestamptz not null default now(),
>   constraint phase_state_singleton_per_user unique (user_id)
> );
> 
> -- seed a row for the current user (run while authenticated in SQL editor)
> insert into phase_state (current_phase_id, last_non_settlement_phase_id)
> values ('02','02')
> on conflict (user_id) do nothing;
> 
> commit;
> ```
> 
> ### Why this matters
> - `current_phase_id` tells the app what phase you’re “in”
> - `last_non_settlement_phase_id` supports “jump to settlement then return”
> - You can change phases from your phone by updating one row
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 2) RLS for `phase_state` (so you can read/write only your row)
> If your RLS file already enables tables similarly, add this:
> 
> ```sql
> alter table phase_state enable row level security;
> 
> create policy "phase_state_select_own"
> on phase_state for select
> using (user_id = auth.uid());
> 
> create policy "phase_state_insert_own"
> on phase_state for insert
> with check (user_id = auth.uid());
> 
> create policy "phase_state_update_own"
> on phase_state for update
> using (user_id = auth.uid())
> with check (user_id = auth.uid());
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 3) Add `workstream` to tasks/docs/drafts (optional, but helpful)
> This gives you “Foreclosure / Credit / Utilities / ADA …” filtering inside any phase.
> 
> ```sql
> alter table tasks add column if not exists workstream text;
> alter table documents add column if not exists workstream text;
> alter table drafts add column if not exists workstream text;
> ```
> 
> No constraints yet—keep it flexible.
>

> ### Gemini Prompt (chunk 1: phase state + gating + settlement jump)

> 
> ```text
> Update the Case Ops React app to enforce an escalation ladder with a settlement jump.
> 
> Rules:
> - Phases come from Supabase table `phases`.
> - Add a new Supabase table `phase_state` with columns:
>   user_id, current_phase_id, settlement_phase_id(default '05'), allow_settlement_jump, last_non_settlement_phase_id
> - The app must read the current phase from `phase_state` (singleton row per user).
> - Users may navigate freely to:
>   (a) any phase with id <= current_phase_id (earlier or current)
>   (b) the settlement phase ONLY if allow_settlement_jump is true
> - Users may NOT navigate to later phases (id > current_phase_id) unless they click "Advance Phase".
> - "Advance Phase" moves current_phase_id to the next numeric phase (e.g., '02' -> '03') and updates phase_state.updated_at.
> - "Jump to Settlement" sets last_non_settlement_phase_id = current_phase_id, then sets current_phase_id = settlement_phase_id.
> - "Return from Settlement" sets current_phase_id back to last_non_settlement_phase_id.
>

> 1) A hook `usePhaseState()` that reads/writes `phase_state`.
> 2) Update phase navigation UI to show locked phases and allow only the rules above.
> 3) Add buttons:
>    - Advance Phase
>    - Jump to Settlement
>    - Return from Settlement (only visible when current_phase_id == settlement_phase_id)
> 
> Constraints:
> - Do NOT hardcode phase names.
> - Do NOT rename unrelated files.
> - Only touch files needed for phase state + navigation. Return file contents with headers // FILE: path.
> ```
> 
> That will force the app to behave like a guided system instead of a free-for-all.

> Add a guard so you can’t insert null user_id even accidentally:
> 
> ```sql
> alter table phase_state
> alter column user_id drop default;
> ```
> 
> Why? Because the default is misleading if you’re seeding in admin context. You *want* inserts to fail loudly unless user_id is provided explicitly (or inserted from the app).
> 
> If you’d rather keep the default for app inserts, keep it — but understand: **seeding from SQL editor requires explicit user_id**.

>   id uuid primary key default uuid_generate_v4(),
>   user_id uuid not null,
>   current_phase_id text not null references public.phases(id) on delete restrict,
>   settlement_phase_id text not null default '05' references public.phases(id) on delete restrict,
>   allow_settlement_jump boolean not null default true,
>   last_non_settlement_phase_id text,

>   settlement_phase_id,

>   current_phase_id = excluded.current_phase_id,
>   settlement_phase_id = excluded.settlement_phase_id,
>   allow_settlement_jump = excluded.allow_settlement_jump,
>   last_non_settlement_phase_id = excluded.last_non_settlement_phase_id,
>   updated_at = now();
> ```
> 
> ### Sanity check
> ```sql
> select * from public.phase_state;
> ```
> 
> You should see **one row**, with:
> - `current_phase_id = '02'`
> - `allow_settlement_jump = true`
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Step 4: Tell Gemini exactly what changed (important)
> 
> Send Gemini **this exact instruction**:
> 
> ```text
> Important schema update:
> 
> A new table `phase_state` exists and is authoritative for phase navigation.
> 
> Table: phase_state
> - user_id (uuid, singleton row per user)
> - current_phase_id (text, FK phases.id)
> - settlement_phase_id (text, default '05')
> - allow_settlement_jump (boolean)
> - last_non_settlement_phase_id (text)
> 
> Rules:
> - The app must read current phase ONLY from phase_state.
> - On first authenticated load:
>   - If no phase_state row exists for the user, create one with:
>     current_phase_id = '02'
>     last_non_settlement_phase_id = '02'
> - Phase navigation must obey:
>   - Only phases <= current_phase_id are clickable
>   - Settlement phase clickable anytime if allow_settlement_jump = true
>   - Jumping to settlement stores last_non_settlement_phase_id
>   - Returning from settlement restores it
> 
> Do not hardcode phase order or names.
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Why this happened (so it doesn’t repeat)
> - Supabase SQL editor does **not** guarantee prior statements ran
> - `auth.uid()` is NULL in admin/editor context
> - We now:
>   - explicitly created the table
>   - explicitly inserted your row
>   - removed ambiguity
> 
> You’re back on solid ground.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Next checkpoint (do **not** skip)
> Once Gemini confirms the app reads `phase_state`, do this test:
> 
> 1. Load app → should land in **Phase 02**
> 2. Click **Settlement** → allowed
> 3. Click **Return from Settlement** → back to Phase 02
> 4. Try clicking Phase 03 → blocked unless you advance
> 
> When that works, **then** we seed Phase 02 tasks & templates.
> 
> Say **“phase_state verified”** once the table + UI both reflect this, and we’ll proceed.

### User
> gemini told me to past this into supabase. BEGIN;

> 

> CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS phase_state (

>   user_id UUID PRIMARY KEY REFERENCES auth.users(id) ON DELETE CASCADE,

>   current_phase_id TEXT NOT NULL REFERENCES phases(id) DEFAULT '00',

>   settlement_phase_id TEXT NOT NULL REFERENCES phases(id) DEFAULT '05', 

>   allow_settlement_jump BOOLEAN DEFAULT FALSE,

>   last_non_settlement_phase_id TEXT REFERENCES phases(id),

>   updated_at TIMESTAMP WITH TIME ZONE DEFAULT timezone('utc'::text, now())

> );

> 

> ALTER TABLE phase_state ENABLE ROW LEVEL SECURITY;

> 

> CREATE POLICY "Users can view their own phase state"

>   ON phase_state FOR SELECT

>   USING (auth.uid() = user_id);

> 

> CREATE POLICY "Users can update their own phase state"

>   ON phase_state FOR UPDATE

>   USING (auth.uid() = user_id);

> 

> CREATE POLICY "Users can insert their own phase state"

>   ON phase_state FOR INSERT

>   WITH CHECK (auth.uid() = user_id);

> 

> COMMIT;

### Assistant
> That script is **mostly fine**, but it has two problems that will bite you immediately:
> 
> 1) **`DEFAULT '00'` for `current_phase_id`** will FAIL unless you actually have a phase with id `'00'` in `phases`. You don’t. Your phases are `01`–`06`.  
> 2) **`allow_settlement_jump DEFAULT FALSE`** contradicts your rule (“the only phase that can be jumped to is settlement if they offer”). You want it **TRUE by default**, then you can turn it off later.
> 
> Also: making `user_id` the primary key is fine, but it means you must create the row from the app (or insert with a real UUID) — the SQL editor won’t have `auth.uid()`.
> 
> Here is the corrected version you should paste into Supabase.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## ✅ Corrected `phase_state` SQL (safe + matches your rules)
> 
> ```sql
> BEGIN;
> 
> CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS public.phase_state (
>   user_id UUID PRIMARY KEY REFERENCES auth.users(id) ON DELETE CASCADE,
>   current_phase_id TEXT NOT NULL REFERENCES public.phases(id) DEFAULT '02',
>   settlement_phase_id TEXT NOT NULL REFERENCES public.phases(id) DEFAULT '05',
>   allow_settlement_jump BOOLEAN NOT NULL DEFAULT TRUE,
>   last_non_settlement_phase_id TEXT REFERENCES public.phases(id),
>   updated_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT timezone('utc'::text, now())
> );
> 
> ALTER TABLE public.phase_state ENABLE ROW LEVEL SECURITY;
> 
> CREATE POLICY "Users can view their own phase state"
>   ON public.phase_state FOR SELECT
>   USING (auth.uid() = user_id);
> 
> CREATE POLICY "Users can update their own phase state"
>   ON public.phase_state FOR UPDATE
>   USING (auth.uid() = user_id)
>   WITH CHECK (auth.uid() = user_id);
> 
> CREATE POLICY "Users can insert their own phase state"
>   ON public.phase_state FOR INSERT
>   WITH CHECK (auth.uid() = user_id);
> 
> COMMIT;
> ```
> 
> ### Why these edits:
> - `DEFAULT '02'` starts you in the escalation phase you said you’re in now.
> - `allow_settlement_jump DEFAULT TRUE` matches “can jump to settlement if offered.”
> - Added `WITH CHECK` to UPDATE for safety.
> - Qualified `public.` so it doesn’t land in a weird schema.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Next: you MUST create your row from the app (recommended)
> Because **SQL editor runs without auth context**, `auth.uid()` is NULL there. Don’t seed `phase_state` in SQL editor.
> 
> Tell Gemini to implement this bootstrap:
> 
> **On app load after session exists:**
> 1. `select * from phase_state where user_id = session.user.id`
> 2. If none, `insert` with:
>    - `user_id = session.user.id`
>    - `current_phase_id = '02'`
>    - `last_non_settlement_phase_id = '02'`
>    - `allow_settlement_jump = true`
> 
> That avoids the “null user_id” nonsense permanently.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## If you insist on inserting in SQL Editor anyway
> You need your real user UUID (from Auth → Users). Then:
> 
> ```sql
> insert into public.phase_state (user_id, current_phase_id, last_non_settlement_phase_id)
> values ('YOUR-USER-UUID-HERE', '02', '02')
> on conflict (user_id) do nothing;
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> ## One more thing (important)
> Your phases table has a CHECK constraint limiting ids to `01`–`06`. So don’t introduce `00` anywhere.
> 
> ---
> 
> If you paste what you have in `phases` for id `05` (what you want settlement to be named), I’ll tell you whether we should set `settlement_phase_id` to `05` or `04` based on your ladder design.

> 
> # 3) Paperless-NGX: finish tagging and pipe into RAG
> 
> You said “over 300k characters in Paperless.” That’s not huge — it’s manageable. The real issue is *consistent metadata*.
> 
> ## Goal
> Every document in Paperless should end with:
> - **Correspondent** (FCFCU, Court, AES, Citizens, HOA, City, DOJ, etc.)
> - **Document Type** (docket, letter, notice, bill, proof, photo, declaration)
> - **Tags** (phase + workstream + entity + event)
> - **Case ID** (CASE_FCFCU)
> - **Immutable Evidence ID** (your Evidence Vault ID if applicable)
> 
> ## The pipeline (practical and fast)
> 
> ### Step A — Define a canonical tag taxonomy (small!)
> Use tags like:
> - `CASE_FCFCU`
> - `PHASE_01` … `PHASE_05`
> - `WS_FORECLOSURE`, `WS_CREDIT`, `WS_UTILITIES`, `WS_ADA`, `WS_SETTLEMENT`, `WS_PUBLIC`
> - Entities: `ENT_FCFCU`, `ENT_COURT`, `ENT_AES`, `ENT_CITIZENS`, `ENT_HOA`, `ENT_CITY`
> - Key events: `EV_WRIT_EXECUTED`, `EV_SERVICE_DEFECT`, `EV_CREDIT_REPORTING`
> 
> Keep it to ~40–60 tags total. More than that becomes ADHD chaos.
> 
> ### Step B — Bulk tag by rules (Paperless workflows)
> Paperless supports:
> - **Document type rules**
> - **Correspondent rules**
> - **Tagging rules** based on:
>   - filename patterns
>   - OCR text contains
>   - source inbox
>   - document type
> 
> Examples:
> - If OCR contains “Writ of Assistance” → tags: `CASE_FCFCU`, `PHASE_01`, `WS_FORECLOSURE`, `EV_WRIT_EXECUTED`
> - If correspondent = “AES Indiana” → tags: `PHASE_03`, `WS_UTILITIES`, `ENT_AES`
> 
> This is how you clear a backlog quickly.
> 
> ### Step C — Export for RAG
> For RAG, you want:
> - doc id
> - title
> - created date
> - correspondent
> - tags
> - full text (OCR)
> - file path / download URL
> 
> Paperless has APIs for this. The best approach:
> - A script that pulls docs + metadata via Paperless REST API
> - Chunks text
> - Embeds into your vector DB (Supabase pgvector is fine, or separate)
> 
> ### Step D — Link Paperless docs to your Supabase `documents` table
> Your `documents` table already has `metadata jsonb`.
> 
> Store:
> - `paperless_id`
> - `paperless_url`
> - `paperless_tags`
> - `paperless_correspondent`
> - `sha256` (optional)
> 
> So your app becomes the “case cockpit,” Paperless is your “document engine.”
> 
> ---
> 
> # 4) What I need to finalize the Paperless → RAG instructions (minimal)
> Tell me which RAG target you’re using:
> 
> - **Option 1:** Supabase `pgvector` (single system, simplest)
> - **Option 2:** Local embeddings store (Chroma/FAISS) + app queries it (more moving parts)
> 
> Given your “phone / library computer” constraint, **Option 1 (Supabase pgvector)** is the best.
> 
> If you say “pgvector,” I’ll give you:
> - the SQL schema for `rag_chunks`
> - the ingestion script outline (Paperless API → chunk → embed → insert)
> - and a minimal query function for your app
>

> - **Option 2 (RAG-first, Paperless is just intake):** RAG pipeline becomes the primary retrieval layer; Paperless remains helpful but not required for “truth.”

> ## A. Phases, tasks, and required templates
> 
> ### Phase 0 — System setup and conventions (one-time)

> ## B. Paperless tagging: how to finish it fast and make it RAG-ready
> 
> You said you have “over 300k characters in Paperless.” That’s not huge in RAG terms, but the *tagging* can still be annoying if you do it doc-by-doc. The trick is **Minimum Viable Metadata (MVM)** + **bulk operations + rules**.
> 
> ### 1) Define Minimum Viable Metadata (MVM)
> For *every* document that should be RAG-searchable, require only:
> - **Document Type (doctype)**: e.g., Court Filing, Order, Notice, Payment Record, Portal Screenshot, Letter, Email, Property, Receipt, Photo, Transcript.
> - **Correspondent**: Court, FCFCU, Servicer, Sheriff, Clerk, USPS, Insurance, You, Opposing Counsel, etc.
> - **Date**: document date (or best-known).
> - **Tags (2–5 max)**:
>   - `phase:intake|timeline|motions|evidence|discovery|hearing|settlement|appeal`
>   - `issue:service|ada|fees|payment|possession|property|jurisdiction|notice`
>   - optional: `status:needs_review|verified|critical`
> 
> Anything beyond that (fine-grain tags) is “nice-to-have,” not a blocker.
> 
> ### 2) Create a tagging “assembly line”
> Run in this order (fastest path to useful):
> 1. **Doctype pass (bulk):** group by obvious type via search filters (PDF vs image; title keywords).
> 2. **Correspondent pass (bulk):** Court vs Bank vs Sheriff vs USPS etc.
> 3. **Date normalization pass:** fix missing/incorrect dates for only “critical” docs first.
> 4. **Issue tags pass:** only for docs that matter (critical path + anything cited in motions/timeline).
> 5. **Status tags pass:** mark `needs_review` vs `verified`.
> 
> ### 3) Use Rules/Auto-tagging (stop doing it manually)
> Even without fancy ML, rules get you 70–90%:
> - Title/filename contains patterns: `order`, `notice`, `return of service`, `writ`, `sheriff`, `ledger`, `payment`, `portal`, `statement`.
> - OCR text contains anchors: court caption strings, “Return of Service,” “Writ of Assistance,” “Default Judgment,” etc.
> - Correspondent inference: if it contains “Marion Superior Court” → correspondent=court.
> 
> ### 4) Batch-tagging tactics that actually work
> - Work from **Saved Searches** (e.g., “untagged doctype,” “missing correspondent,” “status:needs_review”).
> - Only allow one backlog: `status:needs_review`. Everything else must be either `verified` or deliberately excluded.
> - “Critical path first”: if a doc will be *cited* in timeline/motions, it must get full MVM.
> 
> ### 5) RAG readiness requirements (don’t skip these)
> For each document you plan to index:
> - Ensure OCR text is present and not garbage (fix scans where needed).
> - Ensure the **DocID** is stable (Paperless ID is fine).
> - Ensure **metadata is exportable** (doctype/correspondent/tags/date).
> - Decide how to treat duplicates: either ignore or keep both but mark `status:duplicate`.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## C. Feeding RAG + AI helpers: two options and next steps for both
> 
> ### Option 1 — Paperless-first (recommended for your “legal integrity” mindset)
> **What it is**
> - Paperless is the *source of truth* for text + metadata.
> - Your RAG pipeline pulls documents via Paperless API on a schedule, chunks text, embeds, and stores vectors with metadata filters.
> 
> **Next steps (Option 1)**
> 1. **Lock taxonomy**: finalize doctypes + correspondents + tag families (`phase:*`, `issue:*`, `status:*`).
> 2. **Finish MVM tagging** using the assembly line above until:
>    - 100% of “critical path” docs are `verified`
>    - 80–90% of remaining docs have doctype + correspondent + date
> 3. **Build the export contract** (fields you will index):
>    - `paperless_id`, `title`, `created`, `document_date`, `doctype`, `correspondent`, `tags[]`, `source_path/url`, `ocr_text`
> 4. **Implement incremental sync**:
>    - only fetch docs modified since last run
>    - delete/re-embed if OCR text changed materially
> 5. **Chunk + embed** with metadata:
>    - store vectors with `paperless_id`, `chunk_id`, and all tags
> 6. **Add guardrails**:
>    - exclude docs tagged `exclude:rag`
>    - keep a “citation mode” that returns DocID + page refs (when possible)
> 
> **Operational definition of “done”**
> - You can ask: “Show me every document supporting defective service” and the AI returns results filtered by `issue:service` with DocIDs you can cite.
> 
> ---
> 
> ### Option 2 — RAG-first (faster retrieval, weaker governance unless you’re disciplined)
> **What it is**
> - You export all text (Paperless or filesystem), normalize it into your own corpus format, and treat your RAG store as the primary query layer.
> - Paperless remains intake/backup but not the gatekeeper.
> 
> **Next steps (Option 2)**
> 1. **Export corpus** (text + basic metadata) into a simple local structure:
>    - one JSON/MD file per document with front matter metadata
> 2. **Normalize IDs** (stable doc IDs independent of Paperless)
> 3. **Apply lightweight tagging externally**:
>    - tags stored in your JSON/MD front matter
> 4. **Embed + index** immediately (no waiting for perfect Paperless metadata)
> 5. **Create a “metadata repair loop”**:
>    - when AI finds a doc worth citing, you backfill/repair its metadata in your external index (and optionally in Paperless)
> 
> **Operational definition of “done”**
> - You can retrieve everything fast, but you must enforce consistency yourself or the index will drift.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## D. The fastest path right now (what I’d do this week)
> 1) **Create/confirm your MVM taxonomy** (doctype, correspondent, tags: phase/issue/status).  
> 2) **Critical path docs first**: tag them to `verified` and make sure OCR is clean.  
> 3) **Bulk-tag the rest** to at least doctype + correspondent; leave `status:needs_review` where uncertain.  
> 4) Stand up **Option 1 ingestion** (Paperless-first) with incremental sync and metadata filters.  
> 5) Only if you get blocked (API friction, OCR issues), fall back to **Option 2 export** as a stopgap.
> 
> If you want, paste your current **doctype list + tag list** (even rough), and I’ll tighten it into a clean taxonomy that won’t explode into 900 tags by accident.
